Ancient Sword of Yang Zhongbao of the Great Song Dynasty Discovered: The Daixi section of the Hangzhou-Changxing Road is located in a remote mountainous area. Whenever it rains, mountain floods occur, and the road is often damaged. The Water Conservancy Bureau had previously surveyed the river channel from Shangxiapu to Guanshi Village to widen and deepen it. Recently, workers were demolishing the Xiejiang Bridge. A worker found a sword under the bridge. Upon inspection, the sword sheath was damaged. The words "Yang Zhongbao of the Great Song Dynasty" were engraved on the sword. The residents of the village are all surnamed Yang and have a Yang Family Generals Temple. The worker who found the ancient sword has rushed to Shanghai overnight to sell it.

Huizhou 86

Bandit Den Discovered at the Border of Three Counties: In recent years, Qinghua, Tuokou, Hongyuan, Sikou, Gutan, and other places in Wuyuan have been repeatedly robbed by bandits. It is heard that the bandit den is about ten li in size, with place names like Zunli (Jar Inside), Pingli (Bottle Inside), and Wengli (Urn Inside). Mountain sheds are built wherever the mountain terrain is slightly flat. Going from the Tunkengwu of Xiuning Meixi, the three mountain sheds have several hundred families about thirty li away. Initially, the bandits were kiln workers from various provinces, but later, old mountain farmers joined them. After plundering their fill, they all returned to Zunli and dispersed to their respective sheds. When the stolen silver ran out, they would go out to rob again. Recently, Xing, the head of the zoning self-defense group of Qimen County, led a team and more than a hundred hunters to suppress the bandits. However, the bandits outnumber us, and it is feared that victory is uncertain.

Educational News

Important News

Completion of Curriculum Standards for Elementary Schools and Kindergartens 87

丨Limited to Publication Before August 20th... Middle School Group Commences Deliberations丨

Nanjing, 21st – The Curriculum Standards and Equipment Compilation Committee for Primary and Secondary Schools held a group review meeting for the primary school group on the morning of the 21st, followed by a general meeting in the afternoon. All curriculum standards for kindergartens and primary schools were completed. Textual revisions are the responsibility of the Ministry of Education, with a deadline for publication set before August 20th. The middle school group convened a general meeting on the 21st and will continue deliberations on the 22nd. Standards for the three compulsory subjects – Labor, Home Economics, and Physical Education – and middle school electives will also be finalized. The Ministry of Education will host a banquet for all committee members tonight.

Resolutions of the Primary School Group: (1) Approval of the three subjects – National Language, Social Studies, and Health; (2) Addition of three graduation requirements for Music; (3) Addition of "cultivating a scientific attitude" to the general principles; Deletion of the second item in the scope of activities.

Gu Shu-sen chairs the Middle School Group meeting. General opinions on middle school subject review, resolved: (1) For Chinese Language, apart from the credit allocation, which should adhere to the resolutions of the previous meeting, the remaining content should be revised based on the provisional curriculum standards, taking into account the opinions proposed by the group meetings; (2) For English, apart from the credit allocation and time allocation, which should be revised according to the resolutions of the previous meeting, the remaining content should be passed according to the provisional standards; (3) Natural Sciences: Mineralogy should be taught as part of Chemistry, without a dedicated course. The remaining content is passed. Standards for combined-gender classes should be passed as originally proposed; (4) Remove the phrase "(endeavor to surpass the teaching level of junior high school graduates)" from Physics and Chemistry; (5) History A. For the junior high school history curriculum, Chinese History should be allocated six credits and taught in the first year, while Foreign History should be allocated three credits and taught in the first semester of the third year. B. Add "appreciating the unique spirit of nation-building in each country" to the second goal of the junior high school history curriculum, and pay attention to the 72 characters. C. Regarding the outline of junior high school history teaching materials, Zheng He-sheng and three other committee members are appointed to review and revise them, and submit them to the general meeting tomorrow. D. The curriculum for senior high school history and foreign history will be redrafted and reviewed and revised at the next meeting, without being submitted to the general meeting again; (6) Geography, A. For the junior high school geography curriculum, Chinese Geography should be allocated six credits per semester and taught in the second year of junior high school, while Foreign Geography should be allocated three credits and taught separately in the second semester of the third year. B. Revise several sentences in items eight and fourteen of the outline of senior high school geography teaching materials. Completely delete item fifteen, aviation issues. Calculation should be passed according to the review plan.

丨Details of the First Day of the Primary School Group丨 88

Since the Ministry of Education issued the provisional standards for primary and secondary school curricula and instructed various regions to conduct trials as much as possible, many regions have offered opinions on the curriculum standards to the Ministry. Therefore, the Ministry of Education re-selected experts to form the "Curriculum and Equipment Standards Compilation Committee for Primary and Secondary Schools," hoping that the provisional curriculum standards would be recompiled based on the actual trial results from various regions and the opinions of experts, and the word "provisional" would be removed to facilitate formal publication. The primary and secondary school groups of the committee held their first meeting last month and resolved to first submit the curriculum standards for each subject for review, as reported in this newspaper. The 20th marked the date for the second general meeting of the primary school group at the Ministry of Education. The meeting started at 9:00 AM and adjourned at 5:00 PM.

▲Attendees: Shen Lei-yu, Wei Bing-xin, Wang Jin-xin, Li Xiao-nong, Yi Ke-xun, Ni Zhu-hua, Shen Bai-ying, Xue Tian-han, Peng Bai-chuan, Wu Yan-yin, Gu Shu-sen, Xie Shu-ying, Zheng He-sheng, Zhao Ting-wei, Lin Duan-fu, Hu Yan-li, Jiang Xi-cen, Zhu Bao-qin, Jiang Jing-shuang, Shi Ren-fu, Ma Ke-tan, Zhao Nai-chuan, Dai Ying-guan, Li Qing-song were present. Gu Shu-sen chaired, Xue Tian-han recorded, and formalities were observed.

▲Report Items: The chairman reported on the Ministry of Education's organization of the review opinions from the previous general meeting and the sequence of this meeting.

▲Discussion Items: (A) Regarding the subjects (A) National Language: Except for the following issues, all other revisions from the previous review committee were approved. A separate committee will be formed to discuss the following issues: (1) Revision of ordinary and practical writing in the work requirements; (2) Increase of Party ideology materials; (3) Attention to content knowledge; (4) Classification of story content. The members of this subject review committee are Yi Ke-xun, Wei Bing-xin, Wu Yan-yin, Shen Bai-ying, Xue Tian-han, Zhao Ting-wei, Jiang Jing-shuang. (B) Health: This curriculum is being compiled for the first time. A separate review committee will be formed to revise it in detail. The important matters submitted for review are as follows: (1) The third goal is not aimed at children, which is different from other curricula and should be revised; (2) The minimum requirements for hygiene should be made more specific; (3) Track and field is too focused on the development of instincts. The overall physical education curriculum should pay more attention to basic gymnastics training. The members of this subject review committee are Ma Ke-tan, Shen Lei-yu, Ni Zhu-hua, Hu Yan-li. (C) (1) Move the third item of work categories to the first item, and sequentially change the original first and second items to the second and third items; (2) A separate review committee will be formed to revise the work requirements for the first, second, third, and fourth grades, based on the original articles and the revised version of the previous review meeting, and referring to the specific details of trials in various regions. The review committee members are Jiang Xi-cen, Li Qing-song, Li Xiao-nong, Shi Ren-fu, Wang Wei-xin. (3) The chairman reported that before the general meeting, experts in this subject were invited to hold a meeting on the work requirements for the fifth and sixth grades. It was decided that Mr. Li Qing-song, Mr. Zhao Zheng-duo, etc., would first determine the detailed content of social studies based on the one-year trial experience of the Central District Experimental School in Beijing, and then summarize it into general principles, to be completed by August 1st. This general meeting does not need to discuss it. (D) Nature: This curriculum was approved in accordance with the revised opinions of the previous review meeting. (E) Except for the following revisions, all other revisions from the review meeting were approved. (1) The notes in the original work requirements must still be added; (2) The work requirements for abacus should be changed to: the method of dialing beads in the third and fourth grades, the method of positioning, practice of addition, practice of subtraction, practice of multiplication with one-digit multipliers, practice of multiplication with two-digit multipliers. For the fifth and sixth grades, it should be changed to multiplication with multipliers of three or more digits; (3) Add "and pay attention to the familiarity of fingers" under item eleven of the teaching methods; (4) The item "use of thermometers" in the work requirements for the first and second grades should be deleted; (F) Labor: Delete the measures for promoting this curriculum; the rest is approved in accordance with the revised opinions of the review meeting; (G) Fine Arts: Except for the following revisions, all other revisions from the review meeting were approved; (1) The first item of the minimum graduation requirements for primary school should be changed to "able to explain the meaning expressed in a picture depicting ordinary things; (2) Add the fourth item to the minimum graduation requirements for primary school: "able to sketch simple landscapes without major errors"; (3) The third item of the minimum graduation requirements for senior school should be deleted, and the fifth item should be added: "able to sketch or cut and paste simple landscapes and objects without major errors," and the fourth item should be added: "able to apply natural objects to create patterns and simple continuous pictures"; (H) Except for the following revisions, all other revisions from the review meeting were approved; (1) The second item of the minimum graduation requirements for primary school should be changed to "able to sight-sing single melodies in C major"; (2) Add the words "primary school" under "senior" in the first item of the minimum graduation requirements for senior school, and change the second item to "able to sight-sing single melodies in C major"; delete the five words "must be applied" in the fourth item; (3) Delete the measures for promoting this curriculum (B) General Principles: Please review carefully and discuss them at the general meeting on the afternoon of the 21st (C) Kindergarten: Approved according to the original review plan (D) Each review committee is permitted to convene at 8:30 AM on the 21st. Mr. Wu Yan-yin will preside over the National Language Group, Mr. Ma Ke-tan will preside over the Health Group, and Mr. Jiang Xi-cen will preside over the Social Studies Group. A general meeting will be held at 1:00 PM on the same afternoon.

Dr. Cai Le-sheng Returns to China and Arrives in Shanghai 90

▲Former Professor at the University of Chicago in the United States

▲Now Appointed by the National Central Research Institute

▲Included in the Who's Who in American Science

Dr. Cai Le-sheng, a professor at the University of Chicago Graduate School in the United States, is a leading figure in modern psychology. At the World Psychology Conference held in the United States two years ago, he was uniquely invited to present a formal paper, which brought great honor to the academic community in our country. After Dr. Cai obtained his doctorate from the University of Chicago in 1928, he was immediately hired as a professor at the Graduate School, pioneering the path for Chinese scholars to serve as science professors at famous European and American universities. At that time, an American industrial magnate donated eight million US dollars, specifically allocated for medical psychology research. Dr. Cai was appointed as the director of this research project. Under his guidance, five American scholars assisted him in his research day and night. In recent years, the results have been very good. In addition to reporting them in European and American psychology journals, most of the results have been published in the most famous American "Science" magazine in the scientific community. Dr. Cai discovered that the level of intelligence is directly proportional to the amount of a certain vitamin received in the mother's womb and during breastfeeding. Since ancient times, our country has strongly advocated prenatal education. Now, Dr. Cai has proven it using scientific methods, opening a new era in modern education. The Illinois State Government in the United States, in view of the great contribution of this research, specially sent technicians to make a moving picture of Dr. Cai's experiments and show it in various villages and cities. At the same time, the Chicago Tribune, the New York Times, and the London Times in the United Kingdom all provided powerful introductions. Recently, the Who's Who in American Science included Dr. Cai's name and biographical sketch, treating him as an American celebrity. Dr. Cai was quite averse to this. The National Central Research Institute sent letters and telegrams one after another, urging Dr. Cai to return to China to serve the country, so as to avoid employing talents from Chu in Jin. Dr. Cai agreed generously, resigned from his position in the United States, went to Europe for inspection, and then returned to China by ship. It is reported that he has now arrived in Shanghai.

Private Shanghai Girls' Middle School Ordered to Suspend Summer School 91

The Education Society says that the private Shanghai Girls' Middle School on Wenmiao Road, Ximen, Shanghai, did not report to the Municipal Education Bureau in advance when running a summer school. The teachers listed in the enrollment brochure also included those who borrowed names. The operation was particularly inappropriate. It has now been discovered by the Municipal Education Bureau, which yesterday ordered the school to immediately suspend the summer school and report it, so as not to cause delays.

Lin Bao-hua Suffers a Major Defeat 98

▲Doubles Also Lost to Keio

Tianjin, 20th – On the fourth day of the Keio tennis competition, the Tianjin team suffered惨 defeats in the first three days. Lin Bao-hua lost all three matches and was disappointed. His former fame was swept away, so the number of spectators decreased sharply, while the number of Japanese spectators increased sharply. The doubles match started at 4:00 PM, with the Tianjin team Lin Bao-hua and Ma Rui against the Japanese team Yamagishi and Murakami. The first set was 7-5, and the second set was 8-6. The overall average was 2-0, and the Japanese team won. In the singles match, Tianjin team member He Ke-la-si vs. Japanese team member Aoki, the first set was 6-1 and the second set was 6-4. The overall average was 2-0, and the Japanese team won. At 4:00 PM on the 21st, after the Japanese team's technical performance, they will go to Pingjin.

Tianjin, 21st – The Keio tennis team publicly performed singles matches between Yamagishi and Murakami at 4:00 PM on the 21st. The first set was 7-5, and the second set was 6-3. The overall average was 2-0, and Yamagishi won. Later, at the request of the sports community, they competed in doubles with the Tianjin team. The Japanese team Yamagishi and Murakami vs. the Tianjin team Lin Bao-hua and Da Long-qian, the first set was 6-3, the Tianjin team won, the second set was 2-2, and the third set was 7-4, all won by the Japanese team. The overall average was 2-1, and the Japanese team won. The Japanese team will go to Pingjin by train on the 22nd for a match in the afternoon, and will return to Tianjin by train on the 23rd evening, and will return to their country on the Chang'an Maru on the 24th.

The Fudan United Team Smashes the Shanghai College of Commerce 99

| 26 to 19 |

| The Red Light Team Plays Tonight |

Greatly satisfying, in last night's fourth game of the Japanese Shanghai College of Commerce basketball team, the Fudan United team won a resounding victory of twenty-six to nineteen, and everyone was beaming with joy. The referee was Shao Ji.

▲ Superior Technique. The Fudan United team, a joint team from Fudan University, won last night entirely due to its superior technique and seamless coordination, which was dazzling to watch. The three forwards, Mo, Guo, and Lu, skillfully shot through the basket and net, scoring at will. The Japanese team's two coaches, Ueda and Ohashi, both joined the game, otherwise the result would have been even more unimaginable.

▲ Irresistible Momentum. After the score was seven to six in favor of the Japanese team, their performance declined sharply, while the Fudan United team soared upwards. In the first half, the Shanghai College of Commerce only managed to score one point for every six points scored by the Fudan United team, resulting in a score of twelve to seven. In the second half, seeing that the situation was unfavorable, the two coaches of the Shanghai College of Commerce joined the battle, but the Fudan United team continued to win, reaching twenty-four to fourteen. At this point, the Shanghai College of Commerce caught up by four points, and Guo Zhihong scored two more points with a clean shot. Near the end, Guo committed his fourth foul and was ejected from the game. The Fudan United team won with a score of twenty-six to nineteen.

▲ All Claims Completed in the Morning

Anti-Japanese Aid-to-Overseas-Chinese Society Proceeds with Raising Relief Funds 103

▲ The Economic Committee Held a Meeting Yesterday

Since the Anti-Japanese Aid-to-Overseas-Chinese Society resolved to raise relief funds, enthusiastic people from all walks of life have been donating to the collection points in recent days. The Economic Committee also convened a meeting yesterday afternoon to discuss methods and issued the first announcement. The details are recorded below:

▲ Committee Meeting. The first meeting of the Economic Committee was held at 2:00 PM yesterday. Committee members Xu Jiqing, Zhang Gongquan, Qin Runqing, Qian Xinzhi, Wang Yansong, Chen Guangfu, and Xi Yushu attended. Xu Jiqing presided over the meeting, and Ye Weiyi served as the recorder. The meeting proceeded as planned. (A) Report Items: The chairman reported on the responsibilities of the committee and its mission. (B) Discussion Items: (1) Proposal to publish a notice in the newspaper to solicit relief funds. Resolved: Approved. (2) Discussion on the design of the relief fund receipt. Resolved: Approved. (3) Discussion on the number of relief fund receipts to be printed. Resolved: Seventy books will be printed, with each organization receiving ten books, which will be numbered separately. The perforation seal characters used are as follows: (A) "Shi" for the Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce; (B) "Shang" for the Shanghai Bank; (C) "Zhong" for the Bank of China; (D) "Yang" for the Central Bank; (E) "Fu" for the Fuyuan Money Exchange; (F) "Xing" for the Xingye Bank; (G) "Si" for the Four Banks Joint Treasury; (H) "Jiao" for the Bank of Communications. (4) What procedures should the Anti-Japanese Aid-to-Overseas-Chinese Society follow to withdraw funds from the committee? Resolved: A written notice must be submitted, signed and sealed by all standing committee members before payment can be made. (5) How should future meetings of the committee be convened? Resolved: Meetings will be convened in the name of the committee, with the chairmanship rotating among the members.

▲ Fundraising Announcement. The Shanghai Anti-Japanese Aid-to-Overseas-Chinese Society Economic Committee's Fundraising Relief Announcement No. 1 states: The recent instigation by the Japanese of Korean people to massacre overseas Chinese and burn down businesses has resulted in the deaths and displacement of overseas Chinese in Korea, a truly tragic situation. Reports of this brutality are infuriating. After deliberation by the Anti-Japanese Aid-to-Overseas-Chinese Conference, Jiqing and others were appointed as economic committee members. A unanimous resolution was passed at the first meeting convened on the 21st of this month to start raising relief funds immediately. We hope that compatriots and patriots across the country will generously donate to relieve distress and save lives. We are filled with anxiety and await your response with anticipation. The collection agencies are: the Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce, the Central Bank, the Bank of China, the Bank of Communications, the Four Banks Savings Association, the Zhejiang Xingye Bank, the Shanghai Commercial & Savings Bank, and the Fuyuan Money Exchange. Economic Committee members: Xu Jiqing, Qin Runqing, Chen Guangfu, Zhang Gongquan, Qian Xinzhi, Wang Yansong, and Xi Yushu.

After the Telegram to Confiscate Goods, Japanese Goods Are Gradually Affected 104

▲ Telegrams from Ningbo and Other Places to Stop Loading

▲ Dongtang Implements Suspension of Sales

▲ Shandong Business Community Sends Letter Requesting Attention

After the Shanghai Anti-Japanese Aid-to-Overseas-Chinese Society resolved to implement economic severance with Japan and announced measures for dealing with Japanese goods, merchants from various places took advantage of the fact that inspections had not yet been implemented and purchased large quantities of Japanese goods, resulting in the complete sale of Japanese goods stored in various warehouses in Shanghai. General merchants urgently telegraphed Japan to rush shipments to Shanghai, but it was still not enough to meet demand. The market price of Japanese goods rose sharply, and merchants rushed to buy them. Domestic goods also sold well as a result. The number of Japanese goods exported was unprecedented in recent times. Since the Anti-Japanese Aid-to-Overseas-Chinese Society telegraphed party departments and organizations in various provinces and cities on the 20th to implement the confiscation of Japanese goods and began inspections in Shanghai, the people in various places were greatly aroused upon hearing the news. Therefore, starting yesterday, merchants from various places felt apprehensive, fearing that their goods would be confiscated and punished when they arrived inland, so they stopped purchasing Japanese goods. The situation in various places yesterday is recorded below:

▲ Rushing Shipments for Ten Days. All sectors are taking a firm stance in boycotting Japanese goods. However, in order to allow business groups from various places to clear out their previous inventory, they were allowed to clear shipments within these ten days, from the 13th to the 23rd. Therefore, the amount of goods shipped out in recent days has been extremely high. Now that the deadline is approaching, starting yesterday, even more Japanese goods were reported by the Changjiang business group, and the ship ticket offices of various shipping companies were working overnight. Exports from various ships were also delayed by up to twelve hours due to the congestion of goods. The value of goods reported yesterday was even higher than the day before. The various ships were unable to accommodate the volume, and many shipments were rejected. The piers were especially full of kelp. All shipments must be cleared by the 23rd.

▲ Deadline for Suspension of Shipments. Starting on the 24th, ships on the Yangtze River and coastal routes in this port will completely stop loading Japanese goods. According to various shipping companies, no less than one million yuan worth of Japanese goods have been shipped out of Shanghai from the 14th to the present. Today and tomorrow are the last days for shipments. Starting on the 24th, British, Japanese, and American ships in this port will also refuse to accept Japanese goods reported for shipment by Chinese merchants. However, they will still transport goods reported by Japanese customs brokers. Starting on Friday, committees will be assigned to inspect Japanese goods at the piers of various shipping companies to prevent further smuggling and private shipments.

▲ Telegrams to Stop Shipments. Ningbo, Jiaxing, Linghu, and other places have started to prepare for strict inspection of Japanese goods at docks and stations after receiving information from the Shanghai Anti-Japanese Society. It is reported that the transshipment industry in this port received telegrams from the three places yesterday, instructing them to stop shipping goods there, especially in Ningbo, where the efforts are most intense. It is expected that Japanese exports will gradually decrease starting today.

▲ Dongtang Suspends the Market. The Shanghai Sugar Industry Association yesterday notified its members: "Regarding the resolution of the general meeting on July 20 concerning the measures for dealing with arriving and not-yet-arrived Japanese sugar due to the economic severance with Japan, as follows: (1) Resolved, the measures for dealing with arriving and not-yet-arrived Japanese sugar: Resolved, already-arrived Dongtang sugar will be refused acceptance starting today. Orders for goods that have not yet arrived will follow the same actions as other businesses dealing in Japanese goods. (2) Resolved, suspension of Dongtang sugar trading in the market: Resolved, starting from the 20th of this month, Dongtang sugar trading will be suspended in the market and announced in the market." Therefore, Japanese sugar has been absent from the market since yesterday.

▲ Letter Requesting Attention. The Preparatory Office of the Shandong Business Community Joint Association in Shanghai writes: "To the Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce and the Shanghai Anti-Japanese Aid-to-Overseas-Chinese Society: According to our investigation, some traitorous merchants are taking advantage of the nationwide anti-Japanese movement and economic severance to engage in speculative and traitorous business. After your society announced the measures for dealing with Japanese goods, these merchants not only did not reject Japanese goods, but increased shipments; they not only did not return goods, but increased orders. Our enthusiastic compatriots are creating opportunities for traitorous merchants. On the surface, it is a boycott, but in reality, it is promoting Japanese goods. Inferior goods are selling well, and the fault lies with our own people. We hope that your society will pay attention to this and find ways to strictly stop it, so as not to let down the patriotic enthusiasm of all sectors. We await your response with great anticipation."

▲ Business Community Expresses Itself. The Shanghai National Goods Factory Federation yesterday sent a letter to various factories stating: "All sectors in this city are angered by the instigation of Koreans by the Japanese to discriminate against Chinese and massacre overseas Chinese, and have formed an Anti-Japanese Aid-to-Overseas-Chinese Society. The society has resolved to implement economic severance with Japan and has formally issued four measures for dealing with Japanese goods. Some of the raw materials usually needed by various factories are Japanese goods. We hope that you will list the names of these materials so that we can study them and replace them with domestic goods." (Remainder omitted). (1) The 8th Branch of the Special District Citizen Federation held its second executive committee meeting the afternoon before yesterday at 8:00 PM. The chairman was Chen Chuanmao. The resolutions were: (1) Regarding the Anti-Japanese Aid-to-Overseas-Chinese issue, a notice will be issued to the citizens of this district today, the 23rd of this month, to close business for half a day and fly flags at half-mast to commemorate the deceased. (2) Act according to conscience, do not purchase Japanese goods, prepare for economic severance, and persist to the end. (3) Those who have purchased Japanese goods should first register with the Shanghai Anti-Japanese Aid-to-Overseas-Chinese Society and temporarily suspend sales. (4) Those who secretly purchase Japanese goods again with the intention of making exorbitant profits will be severely punished. (5) To expand and promote the realization of residency rights, a letter should be sent to the Citizen Federation to proceed quickly.

American Soldiers Sentenced for Assault 106

▲ Munn Sentenced to Two and a Half Years in Prison

▲ Daniel Sentenced to Two Years in Prison

Corporal Munn, Private Daniel, and Private Kinna, all American soldiers, assaulted and stabbed sewing worker Ma Chengbu and Ju Shixiang at the intersection of Avenue Road and Seymour Road on May 36. Earlier this month, the American military authorities organized a military court to conduct a joint trial. The results of the trial were submitted to Admiral McVay, Commander of the US Far East Fleet, for approval. The US military headquarters on Haifang Road has now received Admiral McVay's reply and announced the sentences yesterday morning: (1) Corporal Munn is sentenced to thirty months of imprisonment for misconduct and will be transferred to the barracks in the Philippines for confinement and hard labor. After serving his term, he will be discharged and deprived of all civil rights. (2) Private Daniel is sentenced to twenty-four months of imprisonment for drunkenness and assault, which damaged military discipline, and will also be sent to the barracks in the Philippines for confinement and hard labor. After serving his term, he will be discharged. (3) Private Kinna was acquitted.

The Case of a Western Constable Shooting a Chinese Policeman on Haig Road 107

▲ The Municipal Government Continues to Negotiate with the Municipal Council

Since the case of a Western constable shooting a Chinese policeman on Haig Road occurred, the Municipal Government, through Secretary-General Yu Hongjun, has been in serious negotiations with the Municipal Council. The Municipal Council sent a letter to Secretary-General Yu on July 3, stating that the case had been handed over to the Police Committee for urgent special consideration. However, as a result, the Municipal Council only agreed to pay the injured Chinese policeman's hospital expenses and disability compensation. There was no clear indication regarding the punishment of the perpetrator, an apology, or a guarantee. Therefore, Secretary-General Yu sent a letter to Mr. Feith, the Director-General of the Municipal Council, yesterday to continue the protest. The two most recent letters between Secretary-General Yu and Director-General Feith of the Municipal Council are recorded below:

▲ Director-General Feith's Letter to Secretary-General Yu. Sir, With reference to your letter of the 23rd of this month regarding the case of a Chinese policeman being shot on Haig Road, I invite your consideration. The case has been considered in detail by the Police Committee of the Municipal Council at a special meeting held on the 8th of this month. Yesterday, the report of the meeting was also discussed at the Board of Directors meeting. After careful consideration from all aspects, the Board of Directors decided as follows: (1) The incident occurred at No. 858 Haig Road. The house faces Haig Road, and access to the house is only possible from that road. Therefore, the Municipal Council's police entry was not inappropriate, especially since they were acting on the request of the lady of the house. (2) Although the evidence on how the incident occurred is contradictory, the Board of Directors believes that if the Chinese policeman had not drawn his gun at the time, the incident could have been avoided. (3) The incident might not have occurred if senior and experienced police officers had been dispatched to the scene. Regarding the third point above, the Municipal Council has considered it and has informed the police department in writing that in order to avoid similar situations from happening in the future, senior and experienced police officers must be dispatched to the extra-settlement roads. We hope that your government will also instruct your Public Security Bureau to take similar measures. In view of the various circumstances, the Municipal Council is willing to pay the injured Chinese policeman's hospital expenses and, if he suffers permanent disability, to provide compensation based on a report, without affecting the Municipal Council's position and denying that the actions of the Municipal Council's police officers were inappropriate. I am sending you this letter to inform you of the handling of the matter and ask you to investigate. Sincerely, Feith, Director-General of the Shanghai Municipal Council.

▲ Secretary-General Yu's Reply to Director-General Feith. Sir, In response to your letter of July 16, regarding the case of a British police officer of your council shooting a Chinese policeman on Haig Road, the Director-General of this government is instructed to reply as follows: (1) The house where the incident occurred is located outside the scope of the extra-settlement road. The police powers exercised by your council on the extra-settlement road are legally unfounded, and in fact, Chinese authorities have never recognized them and have repeatedly protested them. Moreover, the house is located outside the scope of the extra-settlement road, making your council's actions even more unwarranted. Your council's police officer disregarded Chinese sovereignty and acted recklessly, causing the trouble. It is regrettable that your council's superior police officers did not stop him beforehand. Afterwards, it is even more surprising that your board of directors condoned and covered up his actions. As for the claim that access to the house is only possible from the extra-settlement road, which is used as a reason for your police officer to exercise his duties outside the extra-settlement road, I do not know what basis it has. The request of the American woman was inappropriate, and it was even more inappropriate for your council's police officer to accept this extra-jurisdictional matter. The principle is very simple. (2) Your board of directors, on the one hand, admits that the evidence from both sides is contradictory, and on the other hand, speculates that the shooting incident would not have occurred if the Chinese policeman had not drawn his gun. This attitude is regrettable. If the Chinese policeman drew his gun when he did not need to, would he not have retaliated when he was under violent oppression? The injured wrist was the right wrist, and there is evidence that the gun had already fallen to the ground if he had been holding it in his hand, but none of the witnesses mentioned this. Your board of directors may not have noticed this. Even if we take a step back and assume that the police officer did see the Chinese policeman holding a gun, should he have immediately opened fire, firing again after missing the first shot? Does this situation meet the legal requirements for legitimate self-defense? All of these are things that your council should sincerely consider. (3) Your board of directors stated that the incident might have been avoided if senior and experienced police officers had been present at the time, so they proposed that both sides order senior and experienced police officers to be in charge when similar situations occur on the extra-settlement roads. While this government does not want similar incidents to happen again, with regard to the police administration issues on the extra-settlement roads, in addition to reiterating that it is not within the purview of any of your council's police officers to interfere, it has already instructed the responsible bureau to strictly warn its members to handle all matters with caution. (4) Regarding the board of directors' willingness to pay the injured police officer's medical expenses and disability compensation, this government originally requested compensation for damages. It cannot but express its admiration for the spirit of this proposal by your board of directors. However, what must be solemnly stated is that what this government is requesting is a claim for fairness and justice, not just compensation for material losses. Based on the above points, this government hopes that the board of directors will reconsider the matter and provide a satisfactory response to the previous letter's request for punishing the perpetrator, compensation, an apology, and a guarantee, so as to demonstrate fairness and maintain good relations. Please reply accordingly. Sincerely, Yu Hongjun, Secretary-General of the Shanghai Municipal Government.

The Navigation Administration Bureau Officially Takes Over the Customs Agency Authority Today 108

▲ Eight Technicians Appointed as Inspectors and Measurers

After the Shanghai Navigation Administration Bureau was established on the first of this month, it immediately proceeded to take over the authority for ship inspection, ship measurement, and ship registration, which was previously handled by the Customs on its behalf. Director Xi Dingmo and Jianghai Customs Commissioner Merrell negotiated several times, and an agreement was reached yesterday. The official takeover is scheduled for today. The events leading up to this are recorded below:

▲ Successful Negotiations. The Ministry of Communications previously ordered the Navigation Administration Bureau, instructing Director Xi to go to Jianghai Customs to discuss the issue of taking over the agency authority. Later, the Customs responded that they had not yet received the official notice from the Ministry of Communications relayed by the Ministry of Finance, so it was inconvenient to hand over the authority, resulting in a delay. Recently, the bureau received another order from the Ministry of Communications, instructing them to go to the Customs to negotiate. After receiving the order, Director Xi went to the Customs to discuss with Commissioner Merrell, and an agreement was reached yesterday. It was agreed that the authority would be handed over today.

▲ Handover Situation. Today is the official handover date. Jianghai Customs completed all procedures yesterday. Today, they will hand over the files and documents to the Navigation Administration Bureau. The bureau's ship licenses and permits were issued by the Ministry of Communications and will be used from today onwards. However, the equipment for measuring ships, such as the measuring instruments and measuring rulers, are not yet complete, so the Customs will also hand over all the sophisticated instruments to the Navigation Administration Bureau.

▲ Taking Over Officials. The officials taking over the Customs agency authority were appointed yesterday. Zhu Tiankui, Director of the Technical Department, and technicians Huang Shaoqi, Cao Shoulian, Zhou Houkun, Meng Muzhuang, Zou Jiyun, Ding Yanling, and Xu Shipu, will be responsible for inspection and measurement matters. The registration of ships will be handled by the staff of the registration section of the Second Division.

▲ Customs Officials Assist. Because the bureau is just starting to take over, it is not familiar with previous ship matters. For example, in the ship inspection process, the Customs inspection is carried out step by step, so it often takes several days to complete the inspection of a ship. This time, with the takeover, there may be ships that have not yet completed the Customs inspection, and the Navigation Administration Bureau will have to continue the inspection. Therefore, the Customs has specially sent two foreigners to the bureau to assist in handling all unfinished matters. The two foreigners are named Leons and McIntyre, and they are expected to serve for about two or three months.

▲ Procedures and Fees. Mr. Yao Zhaozhi, the Secretary of the bureau, told a Riri News reporter that the handling fees for ship measurement are very low, more than twice as low as the fees charged by Jianghai Customs. The fee structure is as follows: Ships with a gross tonnage of 20 tons or more but less than 50 tons will be charged 20 yuan. Ships with a gross tonnage of 50 tons or more but less than 100 tons will be charged 30 yuan. Ships with a gross tonnage of 100 tons or more but less than 300 tons will be charged 40 yuan. Ships with a gross tonnage of 300 tons or more but less than 500 tons will be charged 50 yuan. Ships with a gross tonnage of 500 tons or more but less than 1,000 tons will be charged 60 yuan. Ships with a gross tonnage of 1,000 tons or more but less than 2,000 tons will be charged 80 yuan. Ships with a gross tonnage of 2,000 tons or more but less than 3,000 tons will be charged 100 yuan. Ships with a gross tonnage of 3,000 tons or more but less than 4,000 tons will be charged 120 yuan. Ships with a gross tonnage of 4,000 tons or more but less than 6,000 tons will be charged 140 yuan. Ships with a gross tonnage of 6,000 tons or more but less than 8,000 tons will be charged 160 yuan. Ships with a gross tonnage of 8,000 tons or more but less than 10,000 tons will be charged 180 yuan. For ships with a tonnage of more than 10,000 tons, an additional 20 yuan will be charged for every 2,000 tons. If the remaining tonnage is less than 2,000 tons, it will be calculated as 2,000 tons. For ships whose capacity is expressed in dan, 10 dan will be calculated as 1 ton.

▲ Navigation Bureau Announcement. The Navigation Administration Bureau will issue an announcement today stating: "This bureau has now transferred from Jianghai Customs and taken over the inspection and measurement of Chinese and foreign ships. Within the areas of Jiangsu, Zhejiang, and Anhui, Chinese and foreign ships that are required to be inspected, measured, registered, and issued licenses should come to the bureau immediately to complete the procedures according to law. This is hereby announced for your information." This announcement.

China Merchants Bureau Applies for Yangtze Wharf Permit 110

▲ Sending Representatives to the Ministry of Communications for Discussions

The Yangtze Wharf, after being sealed by the Ministry of Communications committee, together with the Shanghai Municipal Police Bureau, and subsequently recovered by our country, was previously purchased by the China Merchants Bureau. It is now said that it has been transferred from the Ocean Society. Due to property rights issues, the Bureau plans to apply to the Ministry of Communications for a permit. Details of the meeting and measures are as follows:

▲ Long-term Occupation by Japanese Merchants During the European War, the Yangtze Wharf was confiscated from German merchants by our country. The land and property were purchased by the China Merchants Bureau from the Ministry of Communications. However, it was leased to the Japanese Ocean Society, preventing the Bureau from taking over. During the first rent arrears negotiation, the China Merchants Bureau approached the Ocean Society to take over the wharf, but the Japanese stubbornly refused to hand it over. After the National Government took over the China Merchants Bureau, it also negotiated with the Japanese to request the return of the wharf, but the Japanese still occupied it without yielding. Although the China Merchants Bureau repeatedly petitioned the Ministry to strive for its return, it was ultimately ineffective, and the matter has been delayed for many years.

▲ Meeting for Permit This time, after the Ministry of Communications sealed the wharf and recovered it, and revoked the Japanese merchants' lease rights, the China Merchants Bureau held a special meeting, chaired by Guo Waifeng, with the attendance of all department heads and secretaries. Commissioner Guo presented this case, stating that the Yangtze Wharf property had been purchased by the Bureau long ago, but it had not been recovered due to the Japanese occupation. Now that the Ministry of Communications has sealed the wharf, if the Ministry leases it to others, it will be detrimental to the Bureau's property rights. He asked how to reclaim it for the Bureau's own use and requested a public decision.

▲ Sending Representatives to Request After discussions among the attending department heads and secretaries, it was agreed that this matter should be handled according to property rights, and an application should be made to the Ministry of Communications for a permit. The measures were divided into two steps: (1) The Bureau should first submit a report to the Ministry of Communications, stating that the wharf was purchased by the Bureau and the past negotiations with the Japanese merchants, requesting the Ministry to return the Yangtze Wharf to the Bureau for management; (2) The Bureau should send a commissioner with the case files to the Ministry of Communications to discuss with the Minister and request a permit. It is said that this method will be followed, and a written report will be submitted to the Ministry first, seeking approval.

Ministry of Finance Reduces Unified Tax on Waste Yarn 111

▲ Six Jiao Per Hundred Jin Based on Waste Cotton Tax Rate

The Shanghai Municipal Industrial and Commercial Association Tax Rules Research Committee received a reply from the Ministry of Finance No. 13312 yesterday. A submitted document requested exemption from the waste yarn tax to maintain the established case and alleviate merchants' difficulties. After investigation, since waste yarn is still yarn with considerable use and value, it should be subject to unified tax. However, considering the varying qualities and prices of this type of waste cotton yarn, it is difficult to assess the price separately for each batch. Therefore, it is provisionally approved to handle it flexibly, and it is generously stipulated that a unified tax of six jiao be levied on 100 jin of waste cotton yarn, which is equivalent to the customs duty rate on waste cotton. This fully demonstrates the intention to alleviate merchants' difficulties. It is hoped that all yarn merchants will be notified to comply with the payment and avoid further doubts. This is the earnest hope of the ministry.

New Regulations for the Pharmacy Industry in the French Concession 112

The French Concession Public Bureau recently passed the pharmacy regulations in a board meeting. Key points are summarized below: (Article 1) No one is allowed to operate a pharmacy in the concession without the Bureau's approval. (Article 2) Anyone wishing to open a pharmacy must comply with Article 4 of the Bureau's Classified Business Regulations and apply to the Bureau's Municipal Administration for approval. (Article 3) Pharmacies are divided into three types: A, Chinese pharmacies; B, Chinese pharmacies selling Western medicine; C, Western pharmacies. (Article 4) Graduation diplomas and resumes. (Article 5) All pharmacies are governed by the Bureau's Classified Business Regulations. (Article 6) Anyone operating a pharmacy in the concession without complying with these regulations will be fined from 10 to 100 yuan. Repeat offenders will be fined double and may be dealt with by the competent court. (Article 7) All Chinese and Western pharmacies established before the promulgation of these regulations must apply to the Bureau for approval within six months to continue operations. Also attached is a table of pharmacy business tax rates: (1) Chinese pharmacy business license fee: fixed at 2 yuan per year; (2) Chinese pharmacy business license selling Western medicine: 2 yuan per year, and should pre-pay business tax rates according to the following levels each year: First class 25 yuan, Second class 20 yuan, Third class 15 yuan, Fourth class 10 yuan; (3) Western pharmacy license annual fee of 2 yuan, and shall be prepaid each year at the following rates: First Class 48 yuan, Second Class 38 yuan, Third Class 28 yuan, Fourth Class 23 yuan. (Note) The second part regarding the following regulations is still in draft: (1) Inventory records; (2) Prescription record books; (3) Method of stamping pharmacy brand name on prescriptions; (4) Method of handling heavy prescriptions; (5) Suppression of poisons and anesthetics, etc.

Japanese Merchants Boycott Chinese Hemp Cloth Sales in Korea 114

▲ Extra Attention Should be Paid

The Municipal Chamber of Commerce yesterday sent letters to the local cloth and rough cloth trade associations regarding the Japanese merchants' boycott of Chinese hemp cloth sales in Korea. The letter stated that the Ministry of Industry instructed [the chamber], "Instructing officials, approved by the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, according to the consul stationed in Sinuiju, the clothing of the Korean people still retains the legacy of the Ming Dynasty in our country. Common people admire white and love to use hemp cloth. The number of consumptions each year is worth about 16 million Japanese yen. Among them, local Korean hemp cloth accounts for about 59 percent of the total, worth more than 9.3 million Japanese yen. The hemp cloth imported from our country accounts for about 34 percent of the total, worth more than 5.9 million Japanese yen, which is a large amount. The Japanese are thinking about boycotting this. Now, the Korean Weaving Association is paying great attention to this matter. On the one hand, it guides farmers and promotes hemp planting, intending to increase production. On the other hand, it encourages the government to double the tariffs, intending to reduce imports. However, the doubling of tariffs is restricted by treaties between the two countries, so there is no need to worry. However, the promotion of hemp planting and increased production is the key to pushing out foreign goods. It should not be underestimated. If the manufacturers and sellers of hemp cloth for sale in Korea do not pay close attention to the quality, value, size, and subtleties of hemp cloth, it will inevitably be boycotted and reduced year by year. Two clippings are attached. Please verify and forward them, etc. Correspond, after checking the original newspaper clipping sent, to consult and forward the contents, extract translations, and instruct domestic hemp cloth merchants to be informed. This order, etc." In response to this, the export value of hemp cloth in our country is very large. At this time of fierce commercial competition, extra attention should be paid to the inherent national products of China, and efforts should be made to improve them in order to promote them. Corresponding translations are attached, hoping that you will check and forward them.

Shanghai Finance Bureau Announces Measures for Collecting Donations and Small Silver Coin Surcharges 115

The Shanghai Municipal Finance Bureau believes that the city has a vast area and exchange rates for silver dollars vary from time to time. It is always difficult to obtain appropriate standards for collecting donations and funds. Therefore, nine official articles have been formally established to limit small silver coin surcharges, hoping to achieve consistency in income and expenditure and to demonstrate fairness. It has already been approved by the Municipal Government for promulgation. The measures are excerpted below:

▲ Shanghai Municipal Finance Bureau Measures for Limiting Small Silver Coin Surcharges Article 1: The collection personnel of the Bureau's affiliated agencies shall handle the collection of various donations and taxes, the payment of small silver coin surcharges, and the discount of copper coins in accordance with the following articles, and shall not arbitrarily change them. Article 2: The standard exchange rates for small silver coins and copper coins are stipulated as follows: (A) 300 copper coins are equivalent to one silver dollar (3 copper coins are equivalent to one cent of a silver dollar). (B) 12 jiao of small silver coins are equivalent to one silver dollar. (C) 1 jiao of small silver coins plus 5 copper coins are equivalent to 1 jiao of a silver dollar. Article 3: Those whose donations and taxes are more than one silver dollar shall pay in silver dollars. Article 4: If the total amount of donations and taxes or the odd amount is more than five jiao and one cent, it can be paid in silver dollars, and the collector shall return the balance in accordance with Article 2. Article 5: If the total amount of donations and taxes or the odd amount is less than five jiao, small silver coins shall be paid, and surcharges shall be paid according to the number in accordance with Article 2. Article 6: If the number of jiao to be collected is paid in silver dollar subsidiary coins, it shall not be restricted by Articles 4 and 5 of these measures. Article 7: If the Bureau's collection personnel do not comply with the provisions of these measures and engage in excessive collection and extortion, the donors may report it to the Bureau for investigation and punishment. Article 8: If the market price has special rises and falls, and a new standard price must be set, the items in Article 2 may be revised and announced. Article 9: These measures shall be implemented from the date of approval by the Municipal Government.

Donggang Steamer Hits Reef in Xiamen Waters 117

▲ All Crew Members Rescued

▲ Japanese Ship Carries Them to Xiamen

▲ Donggang Hits Reef Recently, there has been continuous mold rain, and the sea is often foggy, making navigation very difficult. The Donggang, a steamer of the local Chinese merchants, operates on the South China and Fujian waters. This time, it was loaded with cargo and set sail. While sailing off Xiamen, near the lighthouse, it encountered foggy weather. On the 19th, the ship was lost in the fog, lost its course, and there were winds and waves on the sea surface, causing the ship to hit a reef outside the lighthouse. The hull was breached, seawater entered the cabin, and the ship sank, which was very dangerous.

▲ Shipowner Seeks Help After the ship had an accident, the crew, sailors, etc., scrambled to lower lifeboats into the sea in an attempt to escape. The ship had no wireless telegraph, so the shipowner sent out a distress signal, blowing a whistle and firing rockets, hoping that the ships passing by could hear the alarm and come to the rescue. It is said that the ship was fortunately grounded on the reef, so it was not completely submerged in the sea.

▲ Employees Rescued At about 4:00 AM on the 20th, the Lushan Maru, a Nanyang liner of the local Nissin Company, passed by. The Lushan Maru is a Shanghai-Xiamen-Shantou-Guangdong liner. It departed from Shanghai on the 18th and went to Xiamen to unload goods. On the morning of the 20th, while passing through the waters off Xiamen, the fog had cleared. The crew of the ship saw the distress signal, and the shipowner, Nagayama, followed the navigation regulations and sailed to rescue. Near the Donggang wreck, it dropped anchor and lowered the lifeboats to the Donggang reef, rescuing all 40 crew members, sailors, and passengers. They were taken aboard the Lushan Maru and sent to land in Xiamen.

▲ Sent to Xiamen After rescuing these 40 employees and others, the Lushan Maru carried them to Xiamen. When the Lushan Maru arrived in Xiamen, it handed over the crew and sailors to the Japanese Consulate in Xiamen. The Japanese Consulate then notified the Xiamen Public Security Bureau, which sent personnel to receive them. Yesterday, it was heard that the rescued people had arrived safely in Xiamen, and the crew and passengers on board were not injured or left behind.

▲ Loss Situation According to yesterday's telegram, all the cargo on the Donggang ship was submerged. All the shipowners and others barely escaped with their lives and did not carry any luggage or clothing. As for whether the hull can be salvaged, there is no definite news.

Municipal Chamber of Commerce Changes to Branch Office in Wusong 118

▲ Former Chamber of Commerce is Still Striving

The Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce has established a branch office in Wusong, and it began operating at the original site of the Wusong Chamber of Commerce on the 14th of this month. Although the business of the former Chamber of Commerce has been virtually suspended since the seal was seized, the members are still arguing reasonably. Details are as follows:

▲ Zhang Yuchi Resigns as Director The Municipal Chamber of Commerce has repeatedly considered the issue of the director of the Wusong branch office. It must appoint someone who is familiar with the situation of Wusong and trusted by all the merchants and residents of the town to be competent. As a result of the discussion, telegrams were sent to various agencies stating that Zhang Yuchi did not take office because Zhang is the general manager of Wansheng Garden in Wusong and the founder of the Wusong Chamber of Commerce, serving as the vice president and standing committee member of the chamber. Recently, regarding the issue of the separate establishment of the chamber, he and Zheng Shushan, Dong Fei, Wang Yingru, and other members of the chamber are striving for the existence of the chamber. Although the chamber has been suspended, it is still in dispute, so he is unwilling to give up the chamber and take the position of director of the office.

▲ Change to Branch Office The Municipal Chamber of Commerce's establishment of a branch office requires the director to be qualified as a member of the Municipal Chamber of Commerce in accordance with the regulations. However, when the Municipal Business Consolidation Association reorganized the chambers of commerce in the special municipality, the Wusong Chamber of Commerce was not included in the reorganization, and no merchants in Wusong joined the Municipal Chamber of Commerce. Therefore, the establishment of the branch office was inconsistent with the regulations, so it was changed to a branch office. A wooden seal was carved with the words "Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce Wusong Branch Office Seal," which was put into use yesterday and notified to various agencies. The official director of the office has not yet been appointed and is currently being sought. All affairs are still temporarily handled by Sun Mingqi, a staff member of the Municipal Chamber of Commerce.

▲ Attitude of the Former Chamber of Commerce According to Zheng Shushan and Dong Fei, members of the former Wusong Chamber of Commerce, the chamber received a reply from the Central Training Department stating, "All documents are known. After investigation, this case has been handled in accordance with laws, regulations, and precedents, and replies have been sent to the Executive Yuan and the Shanghai Special Municipality Executive Committee for reference. Await the local party headquarters and the competent official agency to resolve it according to law, etc." In response to this, regarding the issue of existence, we are still waiting for a resolution. Upon reading the newspaper, we saw an article stating that the Central Party Headquarters replied to the Executive Yuan, explaining that the Wusong Chamber of Commerce does not need to be established separately. The members believe that the Central Government misunderstood and violated Article 5 of the Chamber of Commerce Law. A telegram was sent to the National Government Central Party Headquarters and the Executive Yuan, Legislative Yuan, Judicial Yuan, and Ministry of Industry on the previous day, requesting separate explanations.

Resolution of the Tea Room Dispute on the Datong Company's Zhengda Steamer 119

▲ Tea Room Wage Disputes

▲ Union Mediation Concludes

The Zhengda Steamer of the Shanghai-Yangtze line, formerly the New Daming Steamer of the Datong Company, which was built after being sunk by a Japanese ship, is dedicated to the Shanghai-Yangtze line (i.e., the Little Yangtze River). Yesterday, it returned to Shanghai from the port of Yangzhou. The tea room staff had a fight over the distribution of alcohol funds, which was later mediated by the Shanghai branch of the Seamen's Union and resolved peacefully. The details are as follows:

▲ Replacement of Head The Zhengda Steamer has a total of 25 tea room staff members, including Zhao Liansheng, the head, who was the deputy head of the tea room on the New Daming Steamer. After the New Daming was sunk, he was transferred to the Zhengda Steamer as the head. Last month, Zhao took leave to return home to repair his house that was blown down by the wind. He returned to the ship for work on the 17th of the previous day, only to see a notice from the comprador Zhu Zuoting that he was dismissed as head and changed to an ordinary worker. The position of head was promoted by deputy head Huang Yunfang. Zhao then negotiated with the comprador and inquired about the reasons for his dismissal. He was told that he often took leave. Zhao reported to the union and requested assistance. The union is currently investigating.

▲ Tea Room Staff Fight Although Zhao Liansheng was dismissed as head, he was still assisting in the work. Yesterday, after the ship returned to Shanghai from Yangzhou, according to the regulations, after stopping, the tea room staff analyzed the aid funds. The head should get one and a half shares. Although Zhao was dismissed by the comprador, because he had not received an order from the union, the workers still recognized Zhao as the head, so all the alcohol funds of half a share were still given to Zhao. Huang Yunfang argued with him. At that time, worker Zhu Zhiting was dissatisfied and quarreled with him, followed by mutual beatings, which was stopped by others. Fortunately, no one was injured.

▲ Union Mediation After Zhu and Huang fought each other, after being persuaded, at 2:00 PM, the Shanghai branch of the Zhao Seamen's Union was mediated by two members of Luo Tang. As a result, both sides compromised. From now on, half of the alcohol funds for the head will be shared equally by Zhao and Huang, and they will help each other in their work. Both sides were satisfied with the solution. Huang was not a member, but is now being introduced to the association by Zhao.

Local News Two

Inside Story of a Love Suicide 123

▲ Ma Alan is Yao Yuying

▲ A Man and Woman United in This Way

▲ The Deceased Left Behind a Wife and Mother

▲ Yao Yuying Found Not Guilty

At midnight on the 11th of this month, in Room 11 of the North Station Grand Hotel at the intersection of Beishan West Road, a man named Ma Shouxiang (also known as Ma Zixiang) and a young woman named Ma Alan (also known as Yao Yuying) committed suicide by poisoning. The man died instantly, while the woman was rushed to the hospital and survived. On the 14th, the French Concession Police Department escorted Ma Alan to the Special District Local Court for questioning. Details of the case have already been reported in this newspaper.

▲ Two Letters From Outside: Since this case occurred,

it has attracted considerable attention from the general public. Recently, both the French Concession Police Department and the Special District Court received letters by mail. The letter received by the police department was signed by Ling Yuanfang and Qian Dongfu, and mailed from 240 Yangjia Bang Road. The letter stated that Ma Alan's real name was Yao Yuying, and her father was a wealthy businessman in Qingdao. The writers requested justice for the deceased. The letter received by the court was signed by a Mr. Guo, who claimed to admire Yao Yuying's character and wished to marry her.

▲ Many Male and Female Spectators: Yesterday morning was the date for the continued

hearing of the case. The police department brought Yao's family members and witnesses, and escorted Yao Yuying to the Second Tribunal of the Special Court. Judge Ge Zhitan presided with Prosecutor Guo Huaipu. The courtroom was packed with male and female spectators. The defendant, Yao Yuying, still had very red and swollen eyes due to the incomplete elimination of the poison. She stood in the defendant's dock.

▲ Returning Home After Husband's Death: First, Wang Yaotang, the agent of the police department, stepped forward and gave a detailed account of the investigation. He stated that after the last postponement of the case, police detectives began a detailed investigation and learned that the defendant's real name was Yao Yuying, 22 years old, from Wuxi. Her home address was 22, Lane 6, Shiqing Road East, North Sichuan Road. Her father's name was Yao Renjie, who ran a coal mine business in Qingdao. His first wife had passed away, and he had married a Yang as his second wife. Yuying was born to the first wife. She had studied at Qingxin School for four years in her childhood. At the age of 17, she was married to Zhu Xiancheng at the arrangement of her parents and suffered severe abuse. After a year and a half, Zhu suddenly fell ill and died. Because Yao could not bear the suffering, she returned to her mother's home a year ago and lived with her stepmother, Yang.

▲ Secret Love Letters: Across the street, at number 20, was the Qunxin Art Studio, opened by Zhang Wentao. Because the premises were small and insufficient, he expanded to number 18. The deceased, Ma Shouxiang, was a technician at the studio, and his office was in room number 18, directly opposite the defendant's bedroom. As a result, they became acquainted. However, the defendant also had a friend named Tao Guidao, who also worked at the Qunxin Art Studio and was a colleague of the deceased. Tao initially had a crush on the defendant. Later, after becoming acquainted with the defendant's stepmother, he often visited the Yao family. However, going alone was inconvenient, so he brought Ma Shouxiang along. Ma Shouxiang, still concerned, first threw a love letter through the window into the defendant's bedroom. After reading it, she expressed sympathy, and their relationship began.

▲ Plotting Suicide at Kunshan: On the 9th of this month, the defendant's father suddenly returned home from Qingdao and saw a man (Ma Shouxiang) with the defendant in the living room. He became suspicious and, in the evening, questioned Yang, learning the whole story. He negotiated with Ma Shouxiang, who wanted to commit suicide, but the defendant dissuaded him. On the 10th, the defendant and the deceased first met in a nearby hotel and decided to go to Kunshan together to commit suicide, to prevent outsiders from discovering the truth.

▲ Going to Fanwang Ferry Together: Because it was late that day, they went to Andong Hotel on Hubei Road to spend the night. They wrote five suicide notes, addressed to the defendant's father, mother, Ma Shouxiang's father, uncle, and friends. The next day, they went out and bought a yuan's worth of opium, two boxes in total. They intended to go to Fanwang Ferry Station to get the train schedule to go to Kunshan to commit suicide. On the way, they dropped the five suicide notes and a park admission ticket into a mailbox. When they arrived at Fanwang Ferry, they could not find the schedule, so they decided to change their plan and go to Zhao Feng Garden to commit suicide. However, the park admission ticket had already been dropped into the mailbox.

▲ Poisoning at a Grand Hotel: They then thought of going to Song Park in Zhabei to end their lives, so they went to a cold drink shop on Avenue Joffre in the French Concession and drank ice cream. They wrote another suicide note and mailed it to their friend. Later, the defendant expressed opposition to committing suicide in Song Park. As a result, they went to Room 11 of the North Station Grand Hotel and committed suicide by taking opium. The defendant took one box first, and the deceased took one box later, etc. Now the defendant's family and witnesses are present, requesting interrogation.

▲ Two Reasons for Suicide: The defendant Ma Alan, also known as Yao Yuying, confessed that her husband, Zhu Zhaicheng, had been dead for several years. Judge Ge asked, "Are the facts stated by the police department's lawyer earlier true?" She replied, "Yes." But this time, Ma Shouxiang initiated the suicide. There were two reasons for his suicide: (1) He suspected that I had another lover and my reputation was not good; (2) Due to economic pressure.

▲ Buying a Yuan's Worth of Opium: The judge also asked, "Did your parents want to marry you to a tailor?" She replied, "I have never met him. Ma and I had already had physical relations. The reasons for his suicide have been explained. My suicide was because I had no other relations with others." Ma initiated the purchase of the opium, a yuan total, buying two boxes. Each of us ate one box. I ate first. "Did you instigate or help Ma Shouxiang commit suicide?" She replied, "No, it was all voluntary." "Was your suicide due to family pressure?" She replied, "No." But the deceased's real name was Ma Zixiang.

▲ Yao Renjie's Testimony: Yao Renjie, 59 years old, from Shanghai, coal business, resident of 22, Lane 6, Shiqing Road East, testified: "My first wife died early, and I only have one daughter, the defendant Yao Yuying. Yang is my second wife, married in 1926. Usually, I had a harmonious relationship with Yuying. Yuying married Zhu Zhaicheng at the age of 17. After Zhu died three years later, she separated from her husband's family and lived with me. On May 22nd, I went to Qingdao to run the coal mine business. On July 9th, I returned to Shanghai. After learning about this matter, because Ma Shouxiang already had a wife and was unable to support her, I did not agree. Unexpectedly, Yuying left the next day, the 10th, without saying goodbye. At first, I only knew that she went to a relative's place. Later, I saw the news in the newspaper and learned about the suicide by poisoning. Now I request permission to take the defendant back, so that I can arrange a marriage for her in the future, etc."

▲ What the Stepmother Said: Yao Yang, 32 years old, from Beiping, testified: "On the 9th of this month, my husband returned home from Qingdao and saw Ma Shouxiang in the living room. He asked me who he was. I replied that he was Yuying's friend. At this time, Ma had already slipped out. Until the next day, Yuying suddenly left. I did not know about the ambiguous relationship between Yuying and Ma at first. One day, I met the wife of a tailor shop owner, who wanted to arrange a marriage for her nephew, a short man named Wang, to marry Yuying. She also told me about Ma Shouxiang. Only then did I learn about it. But I do not know why Yuying committed suicide this time."

▲ Zhang Wentao's Testimony: Zhang Wentao, the owner of the Qunxin Art Studio, testified: "The deceased had been working for me for four or five years, with a monthly salary of fifty or sixty yuan. Tao Guidao had just arrived at my studio last month. On the 17th of last month, because the deceased and Tao were not working effectively, I dismissed them both. The defendant, Yao Yuying, did live next door. But I do not know whether Ma had an ambiguous relationship and why he committed suicide. Ma's original home was in Wuxi. His father passed away last year. Now there is only his old mother, wife, and a daughter at home, etc."

▲ Lawyer's Opinion: At this point, the witness testimony was completed. The police department's lawyer, Wang Yaotang, stepped forward and stated that Ma Shouxiang's suicide was due to two points: (1) Because he was dismissed from his job and faced economic pressure; (2) He had a relationship with the defendant, but the defendant's father opposed it. Moreover, the things they had done were known to almost everyone in the vicinity. Therefore, he discussed suicide with the defendant. According to Article 290, Paragraph 3 of the Criminal Law, those who conspire to commit suicide and commit a crime under this article may be exempt from punishment. Therefore, please adjudicate according to the law.

▲ Yao Yuying Not Guilty: Prosecutor Guo then gave his opinion, stating that according to the Criminal Law, anyone who helps or instigates suicide is guilty, but those who conspire to commit suicide are not guilty. After examining the various aspects of this case, it is indeed a conspiracy to commit suicide, and she should be found not guilty. Judge Ge Zhihao reviewed the report and announced the end of the debate. He declared that Ma Alan, also known as Yao Yuying, was not guilty and ordered that her father take her back.

Dong Yu's Wife Appeals 124

▲ The hearing was held at the Jiangsu High Court yesterday

▲ Dong Kang also attended the court to testify

▲ The original judgment was overturned, and the verdict is pending

Jiang, the wife of Shanghai lawyer Dong Yu, appealed to the Jiangsu High Court to determine her identity and alimony. The hearing was held yesterday. Dong Yu did not appear in court. The appellant, Jiang, and witnesses Dong Kang and Dong Banggan, etc., were all present. Jiang brought a marriage certificate and four letters from Dong Yu to Dong Kang. The letters stated that Jiang was Dong Yu's wife. Jiang demanded cohabitation in court; otherwise, she must be given 10,000 yuan in alimony and a divorce in the name of a wife.
