Thuggish Gangsters in Pudong 125

▲ Beating a Man to Death With Four Fists

Lu Suzhen, from Chongming, had been working as a foreman in various construction plants in Shanghai. Recently, he moved with his family to live in Wujia Ting, Pudong. Due to a minor dispute over moving, he was dragged to a teahouse by local thugs, who arbitrarily extorted money and injured his vital organs. On the morning of the day before yesterday, he died from his injuries. The murderers fled without a trace. Yesterday, his wife reported the case to the police station, who arrested a woman named Shen Yang, who was the instigator. The local bailiff has reported the case to the local court for a post-mortem examination and to arrest the murderers. The details of the investigation are recorded below.

▲ Cause of the Dispute: Lu went to Wujia Ting, Pudong, last month to find a house to rent. He was introduced by a woman named Shen Yang from Haimen, and rented a bungalow belonging to Zhang Aliu. He moved across the river with his wife, Mao (32 years old). After only a month, the house became dilapidated due to thunderstorms. Lu then rented Number 8, Zhu Family Residence in the same area. However, the former landlord, Zhang Aliu, suspected that Shen Yang had been manipulating things from the sidelines because Lu did not state his intention to terminate the lease in advance. He questioned Yang, who did not show any weakness, and was beaten twice by Zhang. This was the cause of the dispute.

▲ Extorting 100 Yuan: After being embarrassed, Yang blamed Lu for not notifying her about the move, and became entangled with Lu. Lu had no choice but to pay five yuan for medical expenses to apologize and settle the matter. However, Yang became greedy, thinking that Lu was a foreman and had plenty of money. She told a nearby thug, Wu Liufu, who gathered more than ten ruffians on the morning of the day before yesterday (the 18th) at 8 AM, dragged Lu to a small teahouse owned by Wu Xu in Wujia Ting, and demanded 100 yuan from Lu. Lu refused, and Wu beat him several times, causing internal injuries to his waist and ribs. As a result, Lu paid Wu and the others 40 yuan to settle the matter.

▲ Dying from Injuries: Lu returned home with internal injuries and took to his bed. He died from his injuries at 10 AM on the 10th. His wife, Mao, had just moved here and was unfamiliar with the area and helpless. She rushed to the accounting office of the construction plant in Puxi to cry and tell Shi Yulin about what happened. Shi was from Haimen and had been working with Lu for many years. He was determined to avenge his friend and immediately crossed the river with Mao to report to the 3rd District Police Station of the Qichang Zhan Public Security Bureau. Chief Shen, at 9 PM that night, supervised the police officers to arrest the murderer, Wu Liufu, who had long since disappeared. He immediately detained Shen Yang, who started the trouble, and the teahouse owners Wu Xu and Zhu Zhang, who were witnesses, and took them to the 3rd District for questioning.

▲ Escorted to Court: First, Lu Mao, the wife of the deceased, 32 years old, testified, "My husband, Lu Suzhen, died unnaturally. I request justice." Next, the first witness, Wu Xu, 39 years old, a local resident, living at 21 Dingjiazhai, who runs a small teahouse, testified: "On the 18th of this month, Shen Yang invited many people to have tea at my teahouse. I saw Lu being punched four times by a man, and then they all scattered. I do not know the murderer. Ask Shen Yang, and she will know." The second witness, Zhu Zhang, 60 years old, a local resident, living at 9 Zhujiazhai, a neighbor of Lu, testified: "On the 18th of this month, Lu borrowed 25 yuan from me, saying that he had been extorted 40 yuan and had already paid 15 yuan. It is true that I lent him the money at that time." Shen Yang also testified, 40 years old, from Haimen, living in Dingjiazhai, Wujia Ting, "I introduced Lu to rent Zhang Aliu's house. Lu moved elsewhere in less than a month, and Zhang said that I instigated it and beat me twice. I was angry and negotiated with Lu. Lu gave me five yuan for medical expenses. Later, I asked Wu Liufu and others to find Lu to talk. I did not tell Wu to beat him, etc." The district chief, considering that the case involved a death, ordered the thousand witnesses to be escorted to the local court for questioning yesterday afternoon. Lu's body was also inspected by the court yesterday afternoon and ordered to be collected, pending the arrest and prosecution of the murderer.

British Engineering Expert Mr. Freeman Arrives in Shanghai 126

▲ Representing the British Dorman Long Steel Company

▲ Establishing a Temporary Office in Shanghai

Mr. Freeman, the Chief Engineer of Dorman Long Steel Company, the most famous British steel factory, recently arrived in Shanghai and established a temporary office at Maolong & Co., 23 Nanking Road. Mr. Freeman's mission is to represent Dorman Long Steel Company in studying China's engineering needs and to consult with key figures on how the company can assist China's construction projects and enhance Sino-British friendship. The company has vast capital and is unparalleled in the world, with numerous coal and iron mines and steelmaking plants in various countries around the globe. Its annual steel production reaches 1.5 million tons, and its steel structures reach 250,000 tons. It specializes in major engineering projects and bridge and railway construction. With its numerous mines, complete equipment, and excellent technicians, even the most difficult and major projects can be managed with ease and without delay. All materials used are produced in-house,廉and reliable. In the past five years, it has contracted engineering projects in various countries worth over 200 million yuan. Its most famous project is the Sydney Harbour Steel Bridge, which is 1,650 feet long, has four railway tracks, and a wide road, making it the largest heavy-duty bridge in the world. Dorman Long Steel Company supplies a large number of steel structures for new construction projects. Important buildings in Hong Kong and Shanghai, such as the Sassoon House and Yokohama Bank, all use its products. Mr. Freeman is a world-renowned engineering expert and has participated in various project plans of the company. This time, he came to China, hoping to contribute to our country.

Merchant Marine School Purchases New Vessel 132

The Wusong Merchant Marine School of the Ministry of Communications has recently decided to purchase a training ship for students' practice. The ship is priced at approximately US$30,000 to US$40,000. This ship is owned by the US Department of Commerce and was originally the Lake Cass, built in 1920. Its load capacity, including fuel, is 4,500 tons, its speed is 9.5 to 10 knots, its length is 325 feet, its width is 44 feet, its depth is 28 feet, its machinery is a triple-expansion engine, it has two decks, four hatches, eight cargo cranes, and its draft is 24 feet when fully loaded. The shipowner wants the ship to be delivered in the United States, while the school wants it to be delivered in Shanghai. Negotiations are currently underway. The ship originally used fuel oil, but after purchase, it will be modified to use both fuel oil and coal, so that students can learn how to use both types of machinery and avoid the difficulty of not being able to purchase fuel at oil-free ports.

Two Notices from the Customs 134

▲ Medicine Packaging Changed for Taxation

▲ Badong Opened as a Port for Steamships

The General Office of the Jianghai Customs issued two notices: (1) After checking, Chinese medicinal materials imported from overseas have always been treated as foreign goods. However, if they are repackaged in Shanghai, they lose their qualification as foreign goods. When declaring for export, they should be treated as local goods and pay export tax. Those that have not been repackaged should still enjoy the benefits of re-export. Please be informed. (2) After checking, Badong, located at the junction of Hubei and Sichuan provinces, has been opened as a place for Chinese steamships to load and unload passengers and goods since July of this year. All Chinese steamships loading and unloading goods there should follow the loading and unloading regulations of the six ports along the Yangtze River. Please be informed to all merchants.

Attempted Suicide by Throwing Herself into the Huangpu River Due to Opium Addiction 135

▲ Fortunately, Ye Zhang was rescued and did not die

Ye Zhang, a woman from Dongting Mountain, 34 years old, lives at No. 16, Yin Xian Alley, inside Dadongmen. Her husband, Ye Shaochu, 46 years old, is doing business in other cities. She is addicted to opium and spends all day lying in bed, smoking. As a result, the money her husband sends home every month is not enough to cover expenses, and she has been facing increasing financial difficulties. Recently, she has become more and more impoverished. Feeling that there is no joy in her life, she suddenly had the idea of ending her life. Yesterday afternoon around 4:00 PM, she walked to the Nanshi Wharf and, taking advantage of people not paying attention, jumped into the Huangpu River. In an instant, waves splashed everywhere. A detective, Wang Anming, from the French Concession General Patrol Department happened to be passing by on business. He saw it and immediately called on the boatmen to rush over and rescue her. She was fortunate to survive. After asking her the reason, he sent her to the First Sub-station of the First District of the Municipal Public Security Bureau. The police chief, Jin, preliminarily questioned her. Considering that she brought the trouble on herself, he gave her some advice and ordered her to stay temporarily while waiting for her family to come and claim her.

Northeast Yearbook Arrives in Shanghai 136

▲ To be sold by Shanghai Pictorial

The 1931 edition of the Northeast Yearbook is a monumental work that has never been seen in the Northeast before. The entire book contains 19 categories, including party affairs, overview, chronology of major events in the Northeast, weather, land, population, administration, military affairs, foreign affairs, judiciary, education, transportation, finance, monetary system, finance, commerce, agriculture, forestry, fishing, animal husbandry, industry, reclamation, immigration, mining, social undertakings, and religion. It contains historical materials, current conditions, and statistics from the Northeast since its inception, all obtained through field investigations. The entire book has 1,500 pages, is 2.5 inches thick, is printed in No. 6 font, and contains more than 2 million words. There are over 100 photographic illustrations. Having this one volume is better than traveling to the four provinces of the Northeast ten times. The book has arrived in Shanghai. The general distributor for Beijing and Shanghai is the Shanghai Pictorial on Wangping Street. The price is 3 yuan per copy. Add 1 yuan for postage. Wholesale prices are 10% off for 5 or more copies, 50% off for 20 copies, and 80% off for 50 copies.

Lady Painter Chen Yufeng Presents Fans 137

Ms. Chen Yufeng, daughter of the renowned Jinling painter Chen Jianhou, is from a family known for their refined artistic talents, and all are skilled in painting. Ms. Yufeng's paintings are especially vigorous, elegant, and refined, and her poems and lyrics are also beautifully charming and worth reciting. In the past, both Wu Changshuo and Li Meian praised her work. Normally, her fees are quite high and difficult to obtain. Now, while traveling in Shanghai, she is responding to requests from various circles by offering a special, lower price for one week, presenting 500 fan surfaces. Each fan surface will only cost two yuan for the ink. Those who love calligraphy and painting should not miss this opportunity. The collection point is Nanyang Hosiery Factory on Nanjing Road.

Bei Kai's New Records to be Released Next Month 138

In recent years, the recording industry has become increasingly developed. The products of Bei Kai Record Company are particularly renowned for their clear and accurate sound. Bei Kai Record Company has already released over two hundred types of records. In Peking opera, they feature famous performers such as Mei Lanfang, Cheng Yanqiu, Xun Huisheng, Xu Biyun, Wang Youchen, Wang Fengqing, Ma Lianliang, Yan Jupeng, Hao Shoushen, Jin Shaoshan, and the recordings sung by Yang Xiaolou are particularly precious and unmatched. It is now reported that this spring, the company went to Beijing and Tianjin to record many new records. Ma Lianliang, Yan Jupeng, Wang Shaolou, Tan Fuying, Tan Xiaopei, Shang Xiaoyun, Xue Yanqin, Du Liyun, Jin Shaoshan, Ma Fulu, Li Duokui, and other famous performers, as well as the drum ballad kings Liu Baoquan and Bai Yunpeng, the comedic drum ballad performer Lao Wagua, and the Henan clapper opera king Jingang Zuan, all have good performances recorded. These new records are expected to be released next month.

Yesterday morning at nine o'clock, the Special District Local Court held a hearing on a case of violating stamp regulations. Judge Tao Dejun fined Lao Xiang Mao Store on Xinzha Road 60 yuan. Ju Tai Chang Silk Store in Minyu Lane, Qiu Chang; Zhongfa Pharmacy on North Mud City Bridge; Fuchangxiang Wine Store on Fujian Road; Guang Sheng Xiang Hosiery Factory at the intersection of Sanma Road and Henan Road; An Kang Silk and Satin Store at No. 13 Tianjin Road; Ruyi Lane Kou Huiyu Silk Georgette Store on North Shandong Road; and Anlihang at the intersection of Dama Road and Shanxi Road were each fined 20 yuan. The Development of Han Lun Beauty Salon 140

Film star Ms. Wang Hanlun has been running her beauty salon for three months since abandoning her film career. At the same time, she also runs a cosmetics business, which is extremely successful. This is because all of the products are secretly made by Ms. Wang herself and contain no lead, which is very different from what is popular outside. Recently, there have been many requests for purchases from other cities, so she is specially seeking agencies in other cities.

Sichuan Fellow-Provincials Association Telegraphs Request to Recover Chongqing Japanese Concession 141

▲ Also Expresses Complete Anti-Japanese Stance on the Wanxian and Xiamen Cases

The Sichuan Fellow-Provincials Association in Shanghai, in order to urge the Ministry of Foreign Affairs to recover the Japanese concession in Wangjiatuo, Chongqing, and hoping that the Chinese people will unanimously oppose Japan, sent two telegrams the day before yesterday, as follows: (Telegram 1) Urgent, respectfully addressed to Minister Wang of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs in Nanjing, upon investigation, the Japanese special administrative concession in Wangjiatuo, Chongqing, was forcibly leased by the Japanese from our local authorities on August 12th of the 27th year of the Guangxu Emperor [1901]. Since the Japanese occupied this concession, they have indulged their military police, brutally killing citizens, such as the Yang Shunfa case and the Tian Jinshan case, which remain unresolved to this day. Their harboring of bandits and harming of the local area, such as selling firearms and smuggling pig bristles, is especially heartbreaking to the people of Chongqing. Now that the central government plans to recover all concessions nationwide, why is the Chongqing people's repeated request to recover this concession being delayed by your ministry? Furthermore, Article 10 of the treaty states that all leases are limited to thirty years, after which the contract should be renewed. According to the regulations, a new contract should be signed every thirty years. According to the date starting from the 27th year of Guangxu, this year, September 24th, marks the end of the thirty-year period. Since the lease has expired, it should be unconditionally recovered. As for renewing the lease, since our country has abolished unequal treaties, there is no room for further recognition. We specially request your ministry to revitalize the spirit of revolutionary diplomacy, implement the declaration of the National Assembly, and recover this concession as scheduled to protect national rights and appease popular anger. Furthermore, the people of Chongqing, deeply resentful of the Japanese's outrageous behavior in Chongqing, have formed a Grand Assembly for the Movement to Recover the Japanese Concession. The public sentiment is high, and the concession must be recovered. According to Chongqing news, the assembly has resolved that if your ministry fails to recover the concession as scheduled, they will use the power of the masses to automatically recover it. Your ministry cannot ignore this matter. If the people of Chongqing act hastily and implement automatic recovery, and are then massacred by Japanese military police or other major incidents occur, who will be to blame? We hope that your ministry respects the late Premier's legacy of abolishing treaties and fulfills the ardent desires of the people of Sichuan. We respectfully submit this telegram, awaiting your wise instructions. Sichuan Fellow-Provincials Association in Shanghai, respectful salute, seal. (Telegram 2) (Omitted titles) To all, the Japanese imperialists have arbitrarily massacred our Chinese people for a long time. Recently, the Wanxian and Xiamen cases have occurred, exposing their ambition and viciousness, which are truly heartbreaking. The people of Sichuan have suffered particularly deeply from Japanese oppression. The Japanese special administrative concession in Wangjiatuo, Chongqing, was forcibly leased by the Japanese from our local authorities in the 27th year of Guangxu [1901]. Chongqing has no other foreign concessions, but Japan occupies this one to control the people of Sichuan. Over the years, they have indulged their military police, brutally killing citizens, harboring bandits, and trampling on the local area, doing everything they want. This September marks the end of the thirty-year lease for the concession. The people of Chongqing, having learned from their pain, have repeatedly requested the Ministry of Foreign Affairs to negotiate for its recovery, but it has been delayed. Recently, the Japanese have increased their military police in the concession area to demonstrate against our Sichuan people in support of the Wanxian and Xiamen cases. Upon hearing this, our association, in addition to telegraphing the Ministry of Foreign Affairs to request that they recover the concession as scheduled, believes that opposing Japan and wiping out the shame has become a movement for our entire nation. Therefore, we offer four points for encouragement to our compatriots nationwide: (1) Recognize the Japanese imperialists as the greatest enemy of our national revolution. We must work hard to defeat them to ensure the survival of our nation. (2) Recognize that Koreans' anti-Chinese sentiment is directed by the Japanese. Firstly, Koreans are Japanese citizens, and secondly, anti-Chinese sentiment is directed by the Japanese. (3) Economic severance with Japan must be maintained until all unequal treaties between China and Japan are abolished and all illegal rights of Japan in China are canceled. (4) Urge the diplomatic authorities to implement revolutionary diplomacy, promptly resolve all pending cases and tragedies between China and Japan, and not engage in secret diplomacy, separating themselves from the people. Compatriots nationwide, opposing imperialism and abolishing treaties are the most important legacies of the late Premier. Now, the Japanese imperialists have placed their knives on our necks. If we still do not vow to oppose imperialism and strive to abolish treaties, how can we face the descendants of the Father of the Nation? We seventy million people of Sichuan will not dare to lag behind you gentlemen, and we will be ready to perish with Japan. We respectfully submit this telegram, asking for your consideration. Sichuan Fellow-Provincials Association in Shanghai, respectful salute, seal.

Liu Maochu Suggests Compassionate Treatment of Prisoners 142

▲ Memorandum to the High Court

Liu Maochu, Chief Prosecutor of the Local Court, submitted a memorandum to the High Court, stating that he was presenting a memorandum on fundamentally improving prisons, hoping for review and implementation. The overcrowding of prisons has been reported monthly and is already well known. The number of cases has surged during the summer seasons, and with many executions, the prisons are overcrowded, with inmates sitting on the floor, suffocating from carbon monoxide. Every visit to the prisons evokes many thoughts. The duty of the prosecutor is to expose crimes, eliminate evil, and not be lenient. For those who disrupt the country and infringe upon public interests, they are brought to justice. The criminal court convicts them, causing them shame, making them pay compensation, restricting their freedom, or taking their lives. Those whose freedom is restricted wear gray clothes, eat coarse food, live in cramped rooms, are separated from their families, and their letters are inspected. Who doesn't have parents and feels heartbroken? Who doesn't have spouses and is constantly dreaming of them? In many cases, a family's livelihood depends on one person, and the wife becomes a servant and the children are sold to other places. The weak commit suicide, and the strong take risks. Secondary problems arise as a result. The reason for this is none other than the problem of people's livelihoods. Driven by the need to survive, people resort to murder, arson, adultery, theft, and other different means. Some are due to a moment of misjudgment, others to a momentary impulse, or they are forced by circumstances. The motives are different, and the situations are pitiable. I have often said that the increase in social crime is primarily due to material civilization, but the country's incomplete education, the imperfection of social systems, and the government itself cannot shirk their responsibility. Furthermore, during imprisonment, on the one hand, they are influenced by what they see and hear, and their bad habits increase, and their knowledge of crime only expands. On the other hand, their personal status is impacted, and they decline further, and few can return to their original state. At the same time, prisoner rations damage the national treasury, using useful rice to feed useless people, which is uneconomical. The way to alleviate the current situation is to grant parole according to law. A slight change during the hot summer is urgent. There are two principles for fundamental improvement: first, in criminal law, if both fines and imprisonment are possible, fines should be imposed; second, in cases of imprisonment, if the conditions for probation are met, probation should be announced. This would increase legal revenue and reduce prisoner rations, benefiting the treasury, and would also allow people to reform, reverse their failures, and allow the weak to escape from their predicament. I, as the Chief Prosecutor, have discussed these two principles during memorial weeks, and they do not violate the articles of criminal law. Before the prisons are expanded, there is no other way, it is said. Chief Prosecutor Liu believes that the latest criminal policy adopts the principle of rehabilitation rather than intimidation and retaliation. It is said that after the Ministry of Justice approves this principle, it will instruct all prosecutors to state their opinions when arguing cases in court to ensure uniformity and avoid discrepancies.

Central Bank Inspection Report 143

▲ Ninety-Sixth

The ninety-sixth inspection report of the Central Bank's issuance reserve states that, in accordance with Article 15 of the Central Bank Regulations, this committee is responsible for inspecting the reserve fund for the issuance of convertible banknotes of this bank. On July 20, 1931, the ninety-sixth inspection was held at the issuance bureau of this bank. The results of the inspection are announced as follows: (A) The total amount of convertible banknotes issued is 36,143,591 silver dollars, including 33,879,454 silver dollar notes and 2,264,137 auxiliary coin notes. The total amount of the convertible banknote reserve fund is 36,143,591 silver dollars, including a cash reserve of 23,775,591 silver dollars. This cash reserve includes 15,818,748 silver dollars stored in the bank's issuance vault, 2,905,564 silver dollars stored in branch banks in various ports, and 5,051,279 silver dollars deposited with fellow banks. The guarantee reserve is equivalent to 12,368,000 silver dollars. (B) The total amount of Customs Gold Unit convertible banknotes issued is 1,000,000 Customs Gold Units. The total amount of the Customs Gold Unit convertible banknote reserve fund is 1,000,000 Customs Gold Units. This reserve fund includes 400,000 US dollars deposited with fellow banks in this port, valued at 4.04 Customs Gold Units. According to Article 2 of the Central Bank's Convertible Banknote Regulations, the cash reserve is 60% and the guarantee reserve is 40%. The results of this inspection show that the cash reserve exceeds 60% and the guarantee reserve is less than 40%, which is in accordance with the regulations. This report is hereby made. July 20, 1931, Chairman of the Supervisory Committee of the Central Bank Li Fuxun, Supervisors Wang Jingli, Bei Songsun, Qin Runqing, Yu Qiaqing, Lin Kanghou, and Xu Jiyin.

Post Office Recruitment of Postal Clerks 144

▲ Preferential Treatment for Women

Regarding the recruitment of postal clerks by the local postal bureau, the bureau received instructions from the Ministry of Transportation yesterday, stating that there are vacancies for postal clerks in the Shanghai, Fujian, Zhejiang, Hubei, Liaoning, and Hunan postal districts, and a total of fifteen people need to be added due to business development. Local recruitment should be approved according to regulations. However, in recent years, many women in various places have received advanced education, and many postal bureau affairs are suitable for women's work, especially in savings and remittance affairs. For the purpose of promoting women's employment, women applicants should be given preferential treatment in this recruitment of postal clerks to show encouragement. This should be followed, and the details of the examination and the names of the recruited employees should be reported to the Ministry for record. According to this order, the postal bureau has decided to give preferential treatment to women who apply for this examination.

Fire at Shoe Store on Fangxie Road 145

▲ Three People Jump from the Building and Are Seriously Injured

At 11:15 last night, a fire suddenly broke out at Lao Tiancheng Shoe Store, No. 196 Fangxie Road, Nanshi, which was opened by Ji Chuchen from Zhenjiang. The fire quickly spread, and fire brigades from various districts rushed to the scene to rescue. It took twelve minutes to extinguish the fire. However, when the fire was raging, Ji's elderly mother, Ding (60 years old), his younger brother A Lin (22 years old), and his sister-in-law Yin (19 years old) all jumped from the building and were seriously injured. They were then taken to Shanghai Hospital by ambulance for treatment.

Chinese Hospital Plans to Expand 146

The Shanghai Chinese Medical Association has established the Chinese Medical College on Huangjiaque Road and attached a Chinese Hospital for students to practice. The hospital doctors are selected by the association from Chinese medicine practitioners with rich knowledge and experience. In case of difficult and serious illnesses, the association can appoint specialists for diagnosis and treatment. With this reputation, the hospital is extremely crowded with patients. The Municipal Social Affairs Bureau has approved factories to send sick workers to the hospital with vouchers for free medicine and treatment. The diagnosis and treatment business has become more developed. In addition, the Factory Law will be implemented on August 1st, and more than a dozen factories have sent representatives requesting that the hospital be contracted to treat their workers. The original wards and clinics are not sufficient and must be greatly expanded to meet the demand. However, the expenses for diagnosis and medicine are huge and cannot be borne solely by the Chinese Medical Association. Therefore, the association has hired Du Yuesheng, Huang Jinrong, Pan Gongzhan, You Jusheng, Wang Xiaolai, Zhang Xiaolin, Ye Huijun, and Fang Jiaobo as directors of the hospital to expand it as much as possible. The night before last, a banquet was held at the Hangzhou Restaurant on Edward Road to entertain the directors and discuss the direction of progress. Du Yuesheng, Fang Jiaobo, and a representative of Pan Gongzhan attended. The standing committee directors of the association gave a detailed explanation of the expansion plan. Work will begin soon, and Shanghai will have a large-scale Chinese hospital to benefit the sick.

Robbery in Hongzhen 147

At around 10:30 the night before last, four robbers suddenly came to the home of Ni Aliu, No. 15 Fanjiacun, north of the Hongzhen branch of the Fifth District Third Police Station. One of the robbers was holding a handgun, all were wearing blue cloth short shirts and pants, and spoke with a northern accent. Before entering the door, the robbers fired three shots to intimidate, and then invaded the inner room, robbing 40 silver dollars and seven pieces of clothing, and fled without a trace.

Women's Temperance Union Prepares to Commemorate Ms. Gordon 148

The Chinese Women's Temperance Union received a letter from the World Women's Temperance Union, stating that the president of the association, Ms. Gordon, passed away on the morning of June 15th of this year at a sanatorium in New York. Upon hearing the news, the members of the association were extremely saddened. Ms. Gordon was kind and devoted her life to the temperance movement, working extremely hard, serving the community, and achieving remarkable results. Women's Temperance Unions in various countries will hold a memorial service on the 21st of this month (Ms. Gordon's birthday). Because the news arrived late in our country, it has been changed to the 25th of this month. Yang Meizhen, Cao Fengxiang, and Pan Ying have been entrusted to prepare for the event.

World Buddhist Academy to Have Tibetan Tripitaka 149

The World Buddhist Academy, established by Master Taixu in conjunction with Buddhist leaders from home and abroad, has its general academy in the capital, and also has facilities in Beiping at the Berlin Temple. Its purpose is to study Buddhism based on Buddhist scriptures in various languages of the world. Yesterday, Taiyuan Fafang and others from the Beiping facility of the academy paid a visit to the Panchen Lama and discussed the purpose of the academy. They were deeply approved and immediately ordered Director Luo of the Panchen Lama's Beiping office to quickly find a complete set of the Tibetan Tripitaka and donate it to the academy for the study of Tibetan.

News from Trade Associations 150

▲ Stone Lime Transportation Industry. The Stone Lime Transportation Industry Association held its first executive committee meeting yesterday. Temporary Chairman Xu Shengfang gave a report. Qiu Zijia, Ma Zhaoye, Xu Shengfang, Lu Fusheng, and Zhou Jinfang were elected as standing committee members, and Qiu Zijia was elected as chairman. The positions of general affairs, accounting, and investigation were appointed, and work began immediately. Next, the proposals were discussed: (1) Stone lime market price issue. It was resolved that from July 20th, the price per load would be uniformly 2.25 silver dollars. If the brick and ash industry trades with cash, a commission of 0.05 silver dollars may be deducted. All members should be notified to comply. (2) It was resolved that if various lime ship companies enter into fixed-order contracts with customers, they should register the contracts with the association within three days. (3) Various lime ship owners reported that when unloading goods at the dock, they were often blackmailed by hooligans. How should this be dealt with? It was resolved that a request should be submitted to the authorities to strictly suppress this. (4) Before the lime ships arrive in Shanghai, they do not know how many ships are already docked at the pier. They often go directly to the port, but if there are too many ships, the Suzhou River current is rapid and dangerous. How should this be avoided? It was resolved that the association would establish a branch office in Bailianjing, Huangdu, where lime ships from the north and south would temporarily register and then be released to Shanghai in order to avoid congestion and danger. The association will also submit a request to the Social Affairs Bureau to notify the local Public Security Bureau to issue a notice of protection. (5) The appointment of the Zhengming Law Firm as the association's permanent legal counsel was approved. (6) The new national standards of weights and measures should be notified to all members to change to the new standards within a time limit.

▲ Embroidery Industry. The Embroidery Industry Association convened an emergency meeting the day before yesterday. Chairman Yang Yongrun opened the meeting as usual. (A) The various reports were completed. (B) The discussion began. (1) The anti-Chinese sentiment of the Koreans is entirely instigated by Japan. According to the Anti-Japanese Aid Association organization, this association should unanimously provide assistance. It was resolved to notify all member stores to fly a half-mast flag for one day on the 23rd, close for half a day, and stop importing Japanese goods and register Japanese goods. The association will certify the claims to show the spirit of the Chinese nation. (2) Business tax is a national tax and should be paid in accordance with the tax law to emphasize tax collection. It was resolved that the collection method would be notified to member stores to comply. (3) The issue of tax exemption for exported embroidery. It was resolved to notify member stores to investigate. (4) The weights and measures reform plan. It was resolved to send a letter to member stores to implement it as soon as possible to emphasize the system and show uniformity. The required supplies should be obtained from the association. Then other cases were discussed and the meeting adjourned.

World Snippets 153

— Sea Guest

Ghosts on the Thames

Western science is prosperous, and culture is developed. It seems that there is no atmosphere of superstition about ghosts and monsters. However, folk beliefs in ghosts are no less than those in the East. And many literati and scholars are studying spiritualism, such as the famous British novelist Conan Doyle, the creator of the great detective Sherlock Holmes. Conan Doyle was very believing in ghosts in his later years and published articles in magazines, creating the theory of ghosts. Recently, a writer named Fox Smith has written a book "The Thames," which describes that there are several places on the Thames River where ghosts appear. Tourists who are afraid of ghosts should not go there. It is said that in the town of Caversham, Berkshire, if tourists camp by the river, they often hear the sound of oars in the middle of the night. When they look closely, there is no boat on the river. But they always hear a boat sailing there. There is also a legend that a female ghost walks across the Abingdon Bridge every night, screaming a terrible "revenge." Some people have even seen her hair floating on the water during the day. This is really incredible. What is especially interesting is a legend in the town of Bisham. It is said that 300 years ago, a very knowledgeable woman lived in the church by the river. She saw that the ink was smudged on her son's writing book and was too dirty. She punished her son, but the punishment was too heavy and he was beaten to death. A few years later, she died in depression. Since then, her ghost has often appeared by the river and in the church, and she washes her hands in the river to wash away her son's bloodstains. These things are nothing more than Qi Dong's wild words and cannot be believed deeply. They can only be used as conversation aids.

Ten Thousand People Mourn the Late General 154

— Baoqin Xuanzhu

General Hu Zhuoru, the former Lieutenant General and Commander of the Fifth Division of the Army, died in action suppressing bandits in Jiangxi. The National Government deemed General Hu a martyr for the country and allocated 50,000 yuan for funeral expenses. A state funeral was held on the 17th at Qingyunpo in Nanchang, Jiangxi, with public memorial services beginning on the 12th. On the first day, over 20,000 officials and guests attended. The public memorial service is described in detail below.

▲ Arrangement of the Memorial Hall The memorial hall was set up in the Zhongshan Memorial Hall in Yuzhang Park. A portrait of General Hu was hung at the entrance of the park, surrounded by electric lights. The railings on both sides were covered with mourning couplets. Inside the memorial hall, another portrait of General Hu was hung, surrounded by white flowers, and embedded with the four characters "Spirit Immortal," formed from electric lights. Below were wreaths arranged in a circular shape. In the center was a sacrificial table, on which were placed offerings of sacrifices, flowers, and fruits, arranged in a solemn manner.

▲ Public Memorial Service The 12th was the first day of the public memorial service. Representatives of the public memorial included He Yaozu, representing Chairman Chiang; Cheng Tianfang and Zhang Daofan, members of the Central Committee; Cao Haosen, a member of the Party and Government Committee; Lu Diping, representing the Provincial Government; Liu Zhenqun, representing the Provincial Party Headquarters; and hundreds of key figures from Party and government organs. (Group guests were outside). After the memorial service, handkerchiefs and portraits of General Hu were distributed. Representatives of the family returned the greeting to the main officiants, expressing their gratitude. He, Lu, Cao, and others shed tears during the memorial service. After the ceremony, they went to the mourning hall to express their condolences to Madam Hu and her son, De Xin.

▲ Memorial Oration by the Commander-in-Chief For this public memorial service, Chairman Chiang of the National Government specially sent He Yaozu as his representative to deliver a memorial oration. The oration read (excerpt): Alas, the four suburbs changed fortresses, beacon fires flew. The dragon and tiger's strategy, spiritedly left a mark on the flag. Saying only the general, deservedly pushed forward the brave. Ten thousand men could not stop. Alone with his horse, fighting battles thousands of miles. Across the clustered mountain peaks, the enemy collapsed at the sight of the wind. A Han in the military. The northwest was pacified. Heroic troops written in grass. The rushing red disaster. Was then given to Jiangxi. Respectfully Xuesang. Directly pounced on the bandit nest. Why did I come later? Same voice with different mouths. Yu Mao Nai De. Selected to ascended the platform. Organized the army and practiced military skills. Killing the enemy was in full swing. The battle of Guangchang. First to climb the flag. Overwhelming nests of ten thousand madnesses. Rain of bullets and a forest of guns. Then you roar like a tiger. Fierce and vigorous. Why did heaven not pity? Lost my great city. Merit is after the people. Danger is before the people. Not arrogant, not boastful. Outstanding virtuous talent. Our national army. Moved the army to the west to conquer. Below vowed to comrades. Above vowed to the vast sky. Vast bright sky. Pacifying bandits is not difficult. Granting me a hundred obedience. Blocking me with many difficulties. Recalling the general. Brave soul is not lost. Grand and majestic spirit. Forever in the sky's destruction. Corresponding to my many lands. Brave and valiant. Reviving my orphans. Reversing the raging waves. Capture the leader, sweep the lair. In one fell swoop, clean up. Work together to the best of our ability. To tell the heroic spirit. Humbly, please accept the offerings.

▲ Filming the Ceremony To highlight General Hu's achievements, the General Hu Funeral Affairs Office hired photographers Yan Bingheng and others from the Shanghai Tianyi Film Company to film the public memorial and state funeral in Jiangxi with a motion picture camera. After filming, the footage was flown to Shanghai for processing. After processing, it was brought back to Jiangxi for screening, to promote his achievements and as a memento.

▲ Lantern Festival by the Chamber of Commerce In addition to following the public memorial schedule and attending the public memorial service, and notifying all shops to lower flags to half-mast to show mourning, all executive and supervisory committee members of the Nanchang City Chamber of Commerce held a lantern festival on the 14th. All kinds of lanterns used were contracted by a certain paper shop, with interlocking designs and novel patterns, which were quite unique, it is said.

Female Education and Female Students Fifty Years Ago 155

— K

This year marks the 50th anniversary of the founding of the St. Mary's Girls' School. A commemorative album was published, with an inscription by Ms. Zhang Mojun. Her account of the situation 50 years ago is quite valuable to look back on. Initially, there was Ms. Emma Jones, who came to China from the United States to preach. She then established a girls' school behind the Hongkou Church, named Wenji. It had eight students, all residing at the school. At that time, there were few women scholars, so they were not only tuition-free but also given money and clothing. Despite these generous treatments, the number of students remained small. Later, during a year of famine, starving people filled the roads. Ms. Jones was able to obtain many more students. However, knowing that they came out of poverty and would leave once prosperity returned, she stipulated that students would not be judged by their level of education but by their age. All students who reached the age of 18, regardless of their level of education, would have to graduate and leave the school. At that time, the curriculum focused on weaving, sewing, gardening, cooking, and other skills. Only in the morning would they briefly read simple versions of the Bible and the Four Books. Some outstanding students began to learn English. Before long, the American Civil War broke out, and the school had no funding. Ms. Jones ordered the students to stop classes and focus on needlework. They sold their work to foreign merchants to maintain the school. Unfortunately, smallpox broke out, and nearly half the school fell ill. Another Ms. Jones took over, but she succumbed to the disease. The school lacked leadership and was closed. When St. John's University built a new school building, Wenji reopened and was renamed as it is known today. The social conservatism of that time and the difficulty of establishing female education are vastly different from today, when women pay huge fees and still cannot gain entry.

Quick Sketch of Hardoon Garden 156

— Mo Yi

In the afternoon of the 19th, my friend Mr. Wang of the She family went to Hardoon Garden to negotiate the matters regarding Hardoon's funeral. I thought of seeing this magnificent Hardoon Garden and followed him. Unfortunately, it was a brief visit, and I didn't get to stroll leisurely, but it broadened my horizons considerably. Here is a random account to show the grandeur of the rich man after his death and the enormity of his extravagance.

As the car turned from Seymour Road into Jing'an Temple Road, I saw the towering paifang (decorated archway) in front of Hardoon Garden, with the characters "East Yuan West Yuan" written on it. The walkways in the garden were temporarily decorated into corridors with white cloth, with countless lanterns hanging. These lanterns were all made of mourning couplets, which was truly innovative. In the center of the garden was a circular lawn with a monument, also made of mourning couplets. At night, electric lights in the monument shone, making it a spectacular sight. The previously colored pillars were now all painted white, like a silver world after snow.

The funeral affairs office was like a small-scale political organization, divided into general affairs, accounting, documents, and other departments. There were many people working there. The servants all wore long summer cloth gowns and were very courteous, which showed they had been trained. I sat for only about half an hour, and tea was changed fifteen times. Each time the tea was changed, a different servant did it. If one knew the number of servants, one might get an astounding number.

Because Mr. Wang was busy, I didn't get to see the memorial hall. However, according to Mr. Wang, the arrangement of the memorial hall was no different from the Confucian Temple's Ding Sacrifice. Bells and drums were placed on both sides, and the ceremony was grand. It was said that during the main sacrifice, Zheng Qinwen of the Datong Music Society, in his capacity as an alumnus of the Cang Sheng University, would join in playing the Zhonghe Shaoyue music. Zhonghe Shaoyue music is used to worship sages. Is Hardoon also a sage now? A smile. The people who performed the dotting of the spirit tablet were three former Qing Dynasty elders: a zhuangyuan (top scholar), a tanhua (third-ranked scholar), and a bangyan (second-ranked scholar). A foreigner's funeral completely using Chinese customs, I had never heard of it before. If there is such a thing, it probably started with Hardoon.

▲ Publishing News The ninth issue of the "Movie Monthly," edited by Mr. Zhou Shixun, was published yesterday by Wenhua Printing House. Also published at the same time was the "Short History of Movie Stars," which contains detailed accounts of the stars' backgrounds, love stories, and so on. It is truly the only reading material for those who love to watch movies from China and abroad.

Travels in India (65) 157

— Ling Hua

The Chinese are good at heresy. Naturally, they follow the Buddhist teachings. However, without traveling to India, one does not know that Buddhism was not conjured out of thin air but was produced based on Indian life and culture. Therefore, those who want to study Buddhism should travel to India once, which is equivalent to studying in China for several years. It must be known that India is the tree of wisdom, and the Buddha is the fruit it bears. There was first Indian culture, and then Buddhism was produced. Otherwise, why was the Buddha not born in China, or in Jewish, Japanese, or Korean cultures, but necessarily came from India, just as Confucius came from China? Knowing people is the only way to discuss the world; discussing the world is the only way to know people. I hope that Chinese Buddhists will not talk about emptiness behind closed doors. One meeting can be opened for every thousand people, and one representative can be elected. Each person can collect five corners, and a thousand people can collect five hundred yuan. Travel to India. From Shanghai to India, 300 yuan will be used as travel expenses, and 200 yuan will be used to purchase Buddha statues and bring them back. This association can be named the Thousand Buddhas Gratitude Association. If everyone can contribute one yuan, then half of it will be saved in the association for global missionary work. If all the Buddhists in the country can contribute one yuan each, half can be used to select people to visit India and half can be used to organize a world Buddhist conference. Then, before long, the entire Chinese culture can hold the bull's ear of the world. It must be known that today's India is not the same as before. The evolving India can also be visited. Contact its scholar-officials, and not only visit Buddhist sites. Those who come should be proficient in English. Otherwise, they will gain less. If you come together, it is enough for one in five people to be able to speak English. When visiting, you can also visit the island of Ceylon, which is an important place of Buddhist influence. In the past, Fa Xian lived here for several years. The main advocates of reviving Buddhism now have branches in the United States and the United Kingdom, but the Chinese are silent and unheard of. Only Master Taixu has traveled the world. However, Master Taixu told me that he planned to organize a Buddhist conference in Bali with 30,000 to 40,000 yuan, but he was unable to do so. One can imagine the stinginess of Buddhists. What is the point of calling oneself a Buddhist if one cannot get rid of stinginess? However, if you travel to Ceylon, you need to use an additional 100 yuan. But the above numbers are the minimum. If anyone comes, the Buddhist Association at 19 Hede Road, Shanghai, can provide accommodation.

That evening, the head of the Naren Misha Church and English teachers revised the declaration of the Asian Cultural Association that I had written. The declaration focused on reviving Eastern culture and opposing war. The language was extremely harsh. It was published in the world under my name. In the text, the civilization of butchers was fundamentally overthrown. In India, the movement is very enthusiastic and is linked to the Gandhi movement. However, Gandhi's academic and charismatic influence is great, and the movement is very fierce. I have been here for several months and have even seen Gandhi, but I still do not fully understand the source of his fundamental dedication to the great movement. How exactly does he fight the British government barehanded and be able to achieve victory to this extent? I asked many people, and they all said that Gandhi is good at silent prayer and has gained the power of the Buddha. They believe in Gandhi as a new Buddha. Try talking to an Indian, and you will be amazed at the greatness and depth of his mental strength. They all say that they have been so influenced by Gandhi's teachings. Indians are good at using mental strength, and Gandhi is a new inventor of mental strength. Looking at the rapid progress of mental strength in all of India, the movement of fighting guns and cannons barehanded seems not without hope. Indians firmly believe that this is possible. However, from the perspective of our Chinese thinking, it seems quite difficult. At first, I thought it was a joke, but recently I have also been influenced by the spiritual environment of the Indians and feel that there is also a two or three-point possibility. However, Indian culture wants to conquer power with conscience. Whether human conscience is reliable is still a question today.

Rotary Club Story

??? (28) 158

— Xu Zhuodai

Ziliang then handed the Romance of the Three Kingdoms to his wife. His wife shook her head:

"You read it to me!"

With no other option, he had to read it to her. This was the third time. Since he wasn't starting from the beginning, he picked a chapter at random and started reading. His wife listened for a while. Was it because she didn't find it interesting? Or was she listening very intently? She closed her eyes. Ziliang read for quite a while, but he didn't hear any sound from her. Could she have fallen asleep? So he stopped reading and gently called her:

"Yueru!"

She didn't respond.

"Yueru! Are you asleep?"

She had really fallen asleep. She wasn't making any sound at all. Ziliang put the Romance of the Three Kingdoms away. He tiptoed toward the attic. It was only seven o'clock, so he could easily correct a few composition notebooks. He had just reached the top of the stairs:

"Thief!"

Ziliang heard his wife's wild scream. How could he not be scared?

"What's the matter?"

"Catch you, this runaway thief!"

After saying that, she laughed loudly:

"Well done! Well done! I wasn't asleep. You ran away instead. You used to tell me: you would never take a concubine. I always thought: as long as I'm not dead, you wouldn't take a concubine. But once I'm dead, I'm afraid it would be inevitable. But judging from your behavior now, you would take a concubine even if I'm not dead. Just think, I haven't fallen asleep yet, and you've already stopped reading the Romance of the Three Kingdoms and sneaked off to the back."

Grains: Hexia Rice Market Suddenly Rises by Three Jiao 167

▲Xinzha. Yesterday, the rice market prices increased, and people's minds were agitated. Due to weather conditions, the shops on both sides took advantage of the situation to purchase inventory. In past years, rice prices invariably rose before the Great Heat (solar term). Sales of thick粳 (japonica), early rice, and late rice increased by two to three jiao. Sales of Luyang tip rice were extremely brisk, and the situation was firm. Bianyin 2 yuan rice arrived in three batches yesterday. All dou (a dry measure for grain) sold out on the same day, and prices were bid up by a chi (a unit of length). Inland boats were unable to enter due to strong winds in the Yejidun area, so imports arrived continuously.

▲Nantou. Sources from all sides were sparse. Although retail sales in urban and rural shops were not strong, prices rose because there was little accumulation of goods. The prices of thick 粳 rice increased by two to three jiao. The arrival of thin稻 (indica) rice was also thin, and the consumption was still low. Fresh goods in this street were still active, and prices also increased by a chi. Sales of Luyang tip rice and foreign rice increased daily and were slightly higher. Sales of Bianyin yuan rice were both sluggish, and there was no demand. Foreign rice dealers and this street continued to have outlets, and the market tightened.

Far-Term Flour Market Opens High 168

▲Mainland Dealers Actively Buying

Yesterday's flour market, although foreign wheat quotations fell by a small amount of about one or two jiao, due to continuous showers and cold weather, various places were suffering from floods, and the early maturing crops that were about to be harvested and the late maturing crops that had not yet been harvested were directly or indirectly affected. Therefore, mainland dealers' buying interest became active again. The prices of far-term months opened higher and higher. However, due to the sluggish actual sales, this month remained flat and weak. As a result, this month was 2.5 li better than the previous day, August was 1.5 fen better, September was 1.25 fen better, October was 1 fen better, November was 10 li better, and December was 1 fen better.

Wheat Market: Futures and Spot Firm 169

Yesterday's wheat market generally showed a firm trend. Although foreign wheat quotations were slightly lower, mainland dealers and the Yangtze River area purchased because various places were suffering from floods, and grain prices were rising. Taking advantage of the trend, they purchased, and their intentions were based on some grounds. However, the operators in this port ultimately believed that the oversupply of foreign wheat had not been resolved, and the future would still be affected by the impact of foreign wheat. As a result, this month was 2 fen better than the previous day, August, September, and October were 1 fen better, November was slightly down by 1 fen, and December was 2 fen better. The spot wheat market remained stable, with little fluctuation compared to yesterday. 2,100 bales of wheat from Danyang, Yangzhou, Nanjing, and Chuzhou were opened and were purchased by Fuxin, Bufeng, and Fengxin. High-quality wheat for delivery to factories opened at 3 taels and 5.5 qian, and the next grade was 3 taels and 3.5 qian.

Silk and Tea: The Opening Price of New Spring Dried Cocoons is Not Cheap 170

▲550 Jin of Reeled Silk Opens at 145 Taels

This year's spring silkworms in Zhejiang Province have suffered from weather damage, and there are few high-quality cocoons and many inferior ones. The yield is extremely poor, and the raw materials for silk factories are scarce. The cocoon market is brisk. Recently, various silk factories have been preparing to start work due to the imminent issuance of silk industry public bonds. They have all begun to purchase raw materials, and demand exceeds supply. Cocoon prices have become increasingly upward. Yesterday, a certain silk factory in Zhabei imported 380 dan of new spring dried cocoons from Hangzhou and Shaoxing. 550 jin of reeled silk opened at a price of 145 taels. The cost of pure silk must be 800 taels per bale, plus the cost of reeling, etc., which amounts to about 1,000 taels.

Factory Silk Exports to Europe Show No Improvement 171

Yesterday, the foreign firms' silk market in this port remained firm. It was found that the export of Shanghai white factory silk to the United States had been stagnant for a long time, and there was no improvement in the sales volume to Britain and France. The market atmosphere was sluggish. Yesterday, only Jardine Matheson and others imported 20 bales of Shanghai white factory silk, and Taihe and others imported 15 bales of white dried silk. Prices were all firm.

Qining Flower Scented Black Tea Exports to Russia Continue to Be Smooth 172

Yesterday, the Russian Assistance Association's interest in importing Qining flower-scented black tea was strong. More than 3,000 boxes were traded throughout the city, with sales prices ranging from 14 taels and 5 qian to 16 taels and 5 qian, a decrease of two to three taels. The market for Luzhuang Zhenmei green tea has not made any significant progress, and tea prices are increasingly declining. However, there is still strong demand from French firms for Zhenmei and Xiumei, and the market inventory is scarce. Market prices rebounded by three to four taels. The market conditions for other tribute tea and pearl tea were all sluggish.

News from Wuyuan Tea is Fragmentary 173

▲Transportation Problems for Boxed Tea. Wuyuan boxed tea is exported from Lehe and Poyang Lake to Jiujiang and then transferred to Shanghai. Last year, Poyang Lake was plagued by bandits, and river transportation was cut off. Most boxed tea was changed to land transportation and transported through Xikou, and then transported from Tunxi and Hangzhou to Shanghai. However, land transportation costs were high, and the procedures were complicated. This year, the banditry in Raole has been slightly quelled, and river transportation is gradually becoming passable. Unexpectedly, the Fangshao communists from the Fujian border invaded Dexing last month, and the Wuyuan and Lehe river routes were cut off again. Various firms, seeing that the Jin Yuanchang boxed tea boatmen were detained and tied up by bandits, were all cautious. They wanted to change to land transportation, but they were also suffering from a lack of porters. They were very hesitant about this transportation problem. Some changed to transporting from Jiangwan and then transferring to Shanghai, but most had to wait for the Gan River to be open for transportation before starting their shipments.

▲The Second Batch of Zhenmei Tea from Big Firms Piled Up. The first batch of Zhenmei tea from this county from big firms has already been shipped to Shanghai one after another. Although there was some activity in removing stems, the selling price was not as good as the early arrival of Tunxi Zhenmei tea, which obtained a better price. Ordinary Zhenmei tea was even more stagnant and unsalable. The market shrinkage was unprecedented. Therefore, the tea firms were all leisurely and slowly manufacturing and shipping the second batch of Zhenmei tea from big firms to avoid price declines due to the accumulation of goods. At the moment, the second batch of Zhenmei tea from big firms in various firms in the county are piled up one after another, packaged into boxes and waiting for shipment. Only a few firms that imported a small amount of tea only made two batches to complete the season, and it is rare to see those that continued to make three or four batches. Except for Jishengchang, Yuanji, Xinji, Yitaiyi, and Yitaixiang, which imported the most tea, the rest will be completed by the middle of next month.

Piece Goods: Goods Sold Before Arrival in Shanghai 174

▲Existing Inventory Already Exhausted

▲Foreign Dealers May Stop Loading Today

The piece goods market has been soaring in recent days. The smoothness of sales is rare in the past. From the outbreak of the anti-Chinese movement in Korea to yesterday, it amounted to 16,000 pieces. Therefore, the existing inventory has been exhausted. Although inspection has gradually been implemented, most of it has already been transported into the mainland. Among them, the Yangtze River basin has a stronger intention to purchase. Sichuan purchased the earliest. Hankou, Jiangxi, Wuhu, and other dealers have been vigorously searching for goods in the past three days. Northern dealers have less interest because if the boycott becomes severe in the future, they can change to directly purchasing from Osaka. Therefore, there have been some resales. The outlets in this street are also unusually enthusiastic. The Shanghai-Hangzhou and Beijing-Shanghai railway stations have large piles of goods. However, inspection has been implemented since yesterday, so they have slightly restrained themselves. On the foreign dealer side, there are also rumors of stopping loading today. Yesterday's market was slightly softer. It is unprecedented for traders to return goods to customs, mainly because the goods were sold before arriving in Shanghai. However, it is also an important reason to urgently seek to sell. Fine broadcloth is almost disappearing. Huxinting, Huanle, and Qianlijv have all been sold out. Baoqiu's broadcloth is priced at 3 qian 9 fen 2.5 li, and the Yangtze River dealers are vigorously searching for it. Moganshan and Lieyan straight tribute cloths are uniformly out of stock. Whether it is large-patterned, medium-patterned, or black-patterned floral cloth, they have all been exhausted. Floral straight tribute wool is even rarer.

North-South Goods: The First Batch of New Daxing Vegetables Has Arrived 175

The first batch of new Daxing vegetables was transported by Zhenbang firms yesterday, totaling 153 pieces. They were immediately displayed for inspection. The quality of the goods varied slightly. The color was still good, but the body was still soft. This is unavoidable in the new season. They were immediately offered for sale, priced at 19.5 to 20 taels. Upon hearing the news, Guangdong dealers immediately purchased more than 70 packages from various firms. Goods with good color were sold for 21 taels, while goods of the next grade were sold for 20 taels and 5 qian to 20 taels. The trend was stable.

Sugar Market: Taikoo Sugar Rises Gradually 176

Yesterday's sugar market reports from the producing areas showed that the spot price of Cuban sugar had not changed compared to the previous report. New York sugar futures fell by 3 fen in September, 2 fen in December, and 1 fen each in March and May of next year. The spot and futures prices of Javanese sugar remained unchanged. The Public Association's scheduled operations for Japanese sugar have effectively ceased. Dutch sugar No. 24 coarse granulated white sugar turned firm again, and the ex-factory price rose to 11 taels and 6 qian, and later to 5 qian and 5 fen, but buying interest was not strong, and the price offered was low, so they held each other and there was no transaction. No. 20 medium granulated white sugar was priced at 11 taels, and the market was also stable. The booking price of Taikoo sugar for August rose by another 1 jiao, and the firms' intention to purchase was very weak. Spot DY mark was priced at 11 taels and 7 qian 5 fen to 8 qian, B Lai was priced at 11 taels and 1 qian, CW mark was priced at 11 taels and 8 qian 5 fen, H mark was priced at 10 taels and 7 qian, and HM mark was priced at 11 taels and 3 qian 5 fen. The ex-factory supply was scarce, and the market was quite brisk. A few hundred bags of locally produced Binghua Qing were offered at a price of 10 taels and 2 qian. The local Shanghai and China brands were also offered, and No. 1 goods were priced at 13 taels and 8 qian. The prices were at the original price, and the market situation was firm.
